From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jun  2 05:27:06 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)
Date: Fri, 01 Jun 2001 23:27:06 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] HTTP service
References: <004001c0eb1a$99bc37a0$8cd4e2d1@daniel>
Message-ID: <3B186B1A.D7E878D1@2cah.com>

Set your part-base back to the default and add this to your defaults.cfg:

[Ftp]
    Enabled=0

This will disable the FTP service in Xitami..

> Daniel wrote:
> 
> Hello, I would like to use Xitami as well as war-ftp server.  This server

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jun  2 13:36:19 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 03 Jun 2001 00:36:19 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] HTTP service
In-Reply-To: Message from "Daniel" <daniel_belisle@sympatico.ca>
 of "Sat, 02 Jun 2001 00:15:03 -0400." <004001c0eb1a$99bc37a0$8cd4e2d1@daniel>
Message-ID: <200106021236.AAA09597@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <004001c0eb1a$99bc37a0$8cd4e2d1@daniel>, "Daniel" writes:
>Hello, I would like to use Xitami as well as war-ftp server.  

You can either tell Xitami not to run the FTP service at all (since it
sounds like you don't need it as you have a separate FTP program):

[FTP]
  enabled = "0"

Or you can change the FTP control port to something other than 21:


[FTP]
  port=XXX

Probably disabling the FTP service is the most appropriate way to go.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

21?

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jun  3 04:19:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (xitami@lists.xitami.org)
Date: Sat, 02 Jun 2001 23:19:26 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Re: Xitami & CGI (was: (no subject))
In-Reply-To: <20010603024954.21693.qmail@web9507.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <200106021236.AAA09597@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>
Message-ID: <5.0.1.4.0.20010602230840.00a815b0@pop.prism.gatech.edu>

At 07:49 PM 02/06/2001 -0700, Dragonballz Insane wrote:
>I would like to know where I can get the program that
>tells the server what to do with a perl or cgi script.
>  I have been told and have experenced that when you
>get ready to run a cgi through an http it comes up to
>be an Internal Server Error can someone help me?

You don't need an external program to tell Xitami how to
handle scripts.  All you need is Perl (or the interpreter for
whatever scripting language you use) and make sure that
Xitami is setup properly.  I've been running perl scripts with
Xitami as my web server for a little under two years with no
problems.  If you're sure you have those things installed
correctly, make sure the script has no syntax errors in it;
check your cgierr.log file to make sure.  Hope this helps.

-Dan Orzechowski
xbonesgt@cc.gatech.edu
http://xbones.resnet.gatech.edu
J is for JAMES, who took lye by mistake.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jun  4 10:31:48 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 04 Jun 2001 21:31:48 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] HTTP service
In-Reply-To: Message from "Daniel" <daniel_belisle@sympatico.ca>
 of "Sat, 02 Jun 2001 14:44:39 -0400." <000601c0eb94$151bbb40$4db8d1d8@daniel>
Message-ID: <200106040931.VAA05313@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <000601c0eb94$151bbb40$4db8d1d8@daniel>, "Daniel" writes:
>Is is possible to have 2 ftp servers to run at the same time and have Xitami
>to run HTTP service on port 80 and FTP service to run on another port than
>21?

Yes.  Change the FTP port setting:

[FTP]
  port=NNN

in your defaults.cfg.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jun  4 10:43:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 04 Jun 2001 21:43:21 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] How to tell Xitami to use a different FTP server
In-Reply-To: Message from "Daniel" <daniel_belisle@sympatico.ca>
 of "Sat, 02 Jun 2001 19:19:39 -0400." <002501c0ebba$7ff0b620$74b6d1d8@daniel>
Message-ID: <200106040943.VAA05792@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <002501c0ebba$7ff0b620$74b6d1d8@daniel>, "Daniel" writes:
>Hello, Is it possible to tell Xitami server to use another ftp server?

You can tell Xitami not to start its FTP server, and then run another:

[FTP]
  enabled = "0"

But you'll have to run the other one yourself; Xitami won't do it
automatically.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>  I need to know if Xitami has a sendmail program 

No, Xitami is a web server, not a postoffice.

> what I should use to fix the $mailprog = '/usr/lib/sendmail'

Depends a whole lot on what you are running X on. On unix, nearly all versions
come with a mail service and something like sendmail. On Windows.... well,
I've had very little fun auto-sending mail in Windows.

What is more interesting is how xitami behaves to that request.....

http://127.0.0.1 -> returns homepage.
http://127.0.0.1/../ -> returns home page.
http://127.0.0.1/../%20/ --> returns a blank directory listing of... //
supposedly ;)
http://127.0.0.1/../%20/../ --> returns home page again.
http://127.0.0.1/../%20/../%20/ -> returns a blank directory listing
http://127.0.0.1/../%20/../%20/%20/ -> returns 404 not found.

3 different methods of responding.....?
Paul

..or you try blat:

package Blat;
use strict;
my($mailer, $server, $Subject, $From, $To, $message);
$server =  "somemailer";# o.s.e
$Subject = "testing blat";
$From = "you\@somewhere.net";
$To = "to\@somewhere.net";
$message = "Hello blat !";
$mailer = "blat - -server $server -f $From -t $To -s \"$Subject\"";
$ENV{"TMP"} = "C:\\TEMP";
open (MAIL, "|$mailer ")or die "Oh shit: $!";
print MAIL $message;
close (MAIL);
=cut
Blat v1.8.2b: WinNT/95 console utility to mail a file via SMTP
by P.Mendes, M.Neal, G.Vollant, T. Charron
  http://www.interlog.com/~tcharron/blat.html
syntax:
  Blat <filename> -t <recipient> [optional switches (see below)]
  Blat -install <server addr> <sender's addr> 
[<try>[<port>[<profile>]]] [-q]
  Blat -profile [-delete | "<default>"] [profile1] [profileN] [-q]
  Blat -h [-q]

-install <server addr> <sender's addr> [<try n times> [<port> 
[<profile>]]]
     : set's SMTP server, sender, number of tries and port for profile
       (<try n times> and <port> may be replaced by '-').

<filename>     : file with the message body ('-' for console input, 
end with ^Z)
-t <recipient> : recipient list (comma separated)
-s <subj>      : subject line
-f <sender>    : overrides the default sender address (must be 
known to server)
-i <addr>      : a 'From:' address, not necessarily known to the 
SMTP server.
-c <recipient> : carbon copy recipient list (comma separated)
-b <recipient> : blind carbon copy recipient list (comma separated)
-o <organization>: Organization field
-h             : displays this help.
-q             : supresses *all* output.
-noh           : prevent X-Mailer header from showing homepage of 
blat
-noh2          : prevent X-Mailer header entirely
-p <profile>   : send with SMTP server, user and port defined in 
<profile>.
-server <addr> : Specify SMTP server to be used. (optionally, 
addr:port)
-port <port>   : port to be used on the server, defaults to SMTP (25)
-hostname <hst>: select the hostname used to send the message
-mime          : MIME Quoted-Printable Content-Transfer-Encoding.
-uuencode      : Send (binary) file UUEncoded
-base64        : Send (binary) file using base64 (binary Mime)
-try <n times> : how many time blat should try to send. from '1' to 
'INFINITE'
-attach <file> : attach binary file to message (may be repeated)
-attacht <file>: attach text file to message (may be repeated)

Note that if the '-i' option is used, <sender> is included in 'Reply-to:'
and 'Sender:' fields in the header of the message.
=end

...or you use MIME::Lite ; in this case adding and compressing an 
attachment:

package myMailTool;
use MIME::Lite;
use Cwd;
use strict;
my($dir,$path,$text,$msg,$From,$To,$Subject,$mailhost,$type,$su
ffix);
$mailhost = "somemailer";
$dir = shift;
$From = 'you@somewhere.net';
$To = 'to@somewhere.net';
$Subject = 'attachment';
$path = getcwd;
$type = 'application/octet-stream';
$text = "someText\n";
$suffix = "\.tar\.gz";
if(!$dir){die "Shit, no directory! $!"}
`tar cvf $dir.tar $dir`;
`gzip --best $dir.tar`;
MIME::Lite -> send('smtp', $mailhost, Timeout => 60);
$msg = MIME::Lite -> new(From => $From, To => $To, Subject => 
$Subject, Data => $text);
$msg -> attach(Type => $type, Path => "$path\/$dir$suffix ");
$msg -> send;
undef $msg;


yours,  Peter


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun  5 16:23:31 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)

Subject: [Xitami] Xitami 2.4d9/Xitami 2.5b5

Xitami Lives!  Long Live Xitami!
--------------------------------

Rumours of Xitami's demise have been greatly exaggerated.  "It's just
been sleeping" said iMatix CEO, Pieter Hintjens.  When questioned he
admited that Xitami was a rather deep sleeper.

Yes folks, it's Xitami release time again.

<music type="cheesy"/>


Xitami 2.4d9 production version and Xitami 2.5b5 beta version
-------------------------------------------------------------

New versions of Xitami are now available from www.xitami.com.  Get them
while they are hot.

Xitami 2.4d9 is now the current production release.  Changes since
Xitami 2.4d7 (Xitami 2.4d8 has been skipped due to version numbering
confusion):

  - A more thorough fix for the "Windows Device Names" denial-of-service 
    problem reported by neme-dhc@hushmail.com to Bugtraq.

  - The Windows GUI and NT Service versions are now open source.  The
    source code is included in the source archives at www.xitami.com.

  - LRWP binary/large files fixes

We strongly recommend sites hosting with Xitami on Windows upgrade to 
Xitami 2.4d9 (after making suitable backups of their existing system).

Xitami 2.5b5 is now the current "beta testing" version that includes 
GSL, a built SSI handler, and more.  Changes since Xitami 2.4b5:

  - A more thorough fix for the "Windows Device Names" denial-of-service
    problem reported by neme-dhc@hushmail.com to Bugtraq.

  - The Windows GUI and NT Service versions are now open source.  The
    source code is included in the source archives at www.xitami.com.

  - LRWP binary/large files fixes

  - The NT Service version should be back "in sync" with the other
    versions, and not suffer from the confusion over "templates or schemas".

Xitami 2.5b5 is NOT recommended for production use.   It is intended
only for experimentation with the new features.  If pain persists, take
two aspirin and call the doctor in the morning.  We have had reports of
problems that will cause Xitami 2.5 to crash, including malformed SSI
pages.  Take care out there.  Look both ways when crossing the street.

However if you want to experiment, we recommend experimenting with Xitami
2.5b5 rather than earlier 2.5 versions.

<music type="jaws"/>


All your favourite bugs lovingly preserved
------------------------------------------

The updates listed above are the only updates that have been made.  "All
your other favourite bugs have been lovingly preserved" said iMatix CEO,
Pieter Hintjens.  "We had developers working night and day to ensure
your favourite bug survived."

This version is the "fix that Windows device names Denial-of-Service
problem, and get everything back in sync" release.  We hope it will be a
safe "drop in" replacement for the existing versions with no hidden
surprises: if it worked before it should work now, and if it was broken
before it should still be broken now. 

We recommend you make a back up before installing the new version, just
in case.  Computers are good at finding surprises where none existed
before.

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

In message <3B1CFB2A.6DD6E408@evernet.net>, david writes:
>open source...does that mean anyone can start helping add
>new features to Xitami??? like ISAPI support??? :-) 

Xitami's always been open source, and we welcome contributions of new
features, code, etc.  Some parts of some versions of Xitami are "value
added" extras, and were closed source -- the Windows GUI/NT Service
portions used to be "value added" closed source extras.  But they're now
open source too.

The Xitami/Pro SSL support is still closed source, as the (small)
revenue from it helps fund Xitami development.  But we're trying to make
the source available for as many of the other bits as is practical.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun  5 16:55:05 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 06 Jun 2001 03:55:05 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Why is my XITAMI server so slow?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jerry Richer" <jerry@chirpingbat.com>
 of "Mon, 04 Jun 2001 08:37:48 -0400." <00a001c0ed41$aef31fc0$6401a8c0@bur.adelphia.net>
Message-ID: <200106051555.DAA22156@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <00a001c0ed41$aef31fc0$6401a8c0@bur.adelphia.net>, "Jerry Richer" wri
tes:
>and HTTP server.  When I call on the FTP server from outside the network it
>is painfully slow.  It takes ten minutes to download a 3.5 Megabyte file
>from the FTP server.  The network is on a cable modem and I am calling in
>from outside the network from a computer that is also using a cable modem.

Most cable modems I've seen are fast for "downloads" (from the Internet
to you), and slow for "uploads" (from you to the Internet).  This makes
them poorly suited to hosting FTP/HTTP servers.  ADSL has the same
problem.

A common speed for the upload side is 128Kbps, which means 16KB/s.
Okay, if you're just sending a request "get me this", but not okay if
you've got to send a large file.

Your 10-minutes, 3.5MB indicates a speed of about 6KB/s, or 48Kbps.
Perhaps the maximum is 64Kbps; or perhaps your cable is busy.  (With
cable you often share the upload speed with others, and sometimes the
download speed too.)

>I realize it's not a XITAMI problem directly but it sure makes
>the FTP and HTTP servers almost useless.

You can eliminate Xitami from the problem by testing on the LAN; it
should be plenty fast there.  If that's the case, then you need to find
out what upload speed your cable connection has, and maybe try to
increase it.  (With the cable I have, the default is 64Kbps or 128Kbps
upload, but you can get faster upload speeds by paying more.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

There're no fixes in there other than the ones listed; which includes
your hack for the VHost problem, etc.  Ie stick with your own version
for now.  Basically we wanted to sort out the build system here again
(it was scattered across a few people's PCs, and is now neatly in our
source control system), and fix the Windows DoS.

Also somewhere between 2.4d7 and 2.4d9 (and 2.5b4 and 2.5b5) we've
retired all our OS/2 machines, so don't actually have a way to build an
OS/2 binary!  (Hence the website dosen't have an updated OS/2 binary
version; just updated source for OS/2.  Fortunately due to the
difference in code to handle device names in OS/2 and Windows, the
problem didn't really affect OS/2 much.)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun  5 19:56:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dennis G. Wicks)
Date: Tue, 5 Jun 2001 11:56:57 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Using perl cgi on NT
In-Reply-To: Ewen McNeill <ewen@imatix.com>
 'Re: [Xitami] Using perl cgi on NT' (Jun  6,  3:56)
Message-ID: <200106051656.JAA14436@eskimo.com>

Greetings;

Yes, there were errors in the log. Exactly as I would expect from
what I discovered yesterday after Matt started me thinking in a 
different direction.

Perl is passed the full path to the cgi script, and that had a space
in it. OK for windows, not OK for perl!

And thanks to Xitami's ability to be reconfigured almost as fast as
you can click the mouse, I found out a few other interesting things.

Unlike a well known server Xitami doesn't care what the script name is.
(The other server requires a cgi extension in some configurations.)
And, perl will accept any valid windows path, except for the above
problem ... No Spaces! Verylongdirectorynames and very.long.file.names
cause no problem. There may be a max length path restriction but I
did not encounter it.

Happy Xitami-ing!
Dennis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun  6 15:52:30 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 07 Jun 2001 02:52:30 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] FREEZE WINOLDAP DISPLAYED WIN98
In-Reply-To: Message from <atvars@bestway.com.br>
 of "Sun, 27 May 2001 18:14:00 GMT." <200105271814.f4RIDxt17294@voyager.bestway.com.br>
Message-ID: <200106061452.CAA02343@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <200105271814.f4RIDxt17294@voyager.bestway.com.br>, atvars@bestway.co
m.br writes:
>   I am experiencing many problems with winoldap process.
>   I use xitami 2.5b4 and some perl cgi applications (perl from activestate). 
>I have zonealarm firewall activated (update version) and vscan (also update 
>version). I am running in P3 with windows 98 se.
>   I started do have many problems of xitami freezing. 

When Xitami "freezes" what is happening?  Is a CGI being started?  From
your description it sounds like you've got a virus scanner checking each
thing that gets run (including CGIs started by Xitami), and perhaps also
ZoneAlarm checking things that are running too.  Given that when you
have these turned off, you don't have the problem, perhaps one or both
of them is intercepting Xitami's attemmpts to run CGIs, etc?

Generally I'd say you'd be better off not scanning things Xitami runs as
they are run, but just scanning the files when you put them on the
machine.  And if you want to run CGIs, you'll have to configure any
security products you might have installed to allow Xitami to start them
automatically.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun  6 15:58:31 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 07 Jun 2001 02:58:31 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami 2.5b4 sends periods as '%2E' in filenames
In-Reply-To: Message from "Rod B. Nussbaumer" <bomr@trmail.triumf.ca>
 of "Wed, 30 May 2001 08:08:06 MST." <3B150CD6.A420E427@trmail.triumf.ca>
Message-ID: <200106061458.CAA02429@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3B150CD6.A420E427@trmail.triumf.ca>, "Rod B. Nussbaumer" writes:
>I've recently upgraded to 2.5b4 on Win95 (!), and now whenever 
>I try to download files from it using either the FTP server or 
>using an http: URL, the FTP client or browser sees the download 
>filename as one long name with the period(s) represented as %2E, 

This happens when downloading a file out of a Xitami-generated directory
listing?  In which case it sounds like Xitami is being a touch too
paranoid about escaping the filenames.

You might want to experiment with changing httpdir.gsl; there are two
versions of each filename passed in: one for display, and one that has
been "escaped" to solve any problem characters.  The latter is used in
the URL by default.  You could experiment with changing it to use the
unescaped name, and see if that avoids your issue.  (It may introduce
other issues though, especially if you have filenames with spaces in
them, etc).

I'll put this on the bug list for more investigation.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>What is more interesting is how xitami behaves to that request.....
>http://127.0.0.1 -> returns homepage.
>http://127.0.0.1/../ -> returns home page.

".." like strings get eliminated before trying to figure out what the
URL means; it's a security measure.  However there seems to be some
strange interaction between encoded spaces and other things going on;
I've put it on the bug list.

>From what I've heard to date this isn't a security issue (since you
don't get access to anything you'd not otherwise have access to, and
even when you do get a directory listing that perhaps you shouldn't
have received, it is empty revealing nothing). 

But it's definitely a strange bug to investigate.

Subject: [Xitami] Running Xitami as a service under Win9x
Message-ID: <42119@dsl.co.uk>

At work (I teach in a university) we've just decided to set up a class
using Xitami (and InstantASP from Halcyon Soft) to replace an exercise
that used to be done under IIS.

So last week I collected the Windows version of Xitami 2.4d7, and
installed it yesterday (on one trial machine).

The first thought that occurred to me was that it ought to be possible to
run it as a service, rather than just auto-running it once someone has
logged in.  I looked through the FAQ - no mention.  I also saw this
mailing list described, and have been subscribed to it for 24 hours.

I *did* try moving the item that gets generated under the
...\CurrentVersion\Run registry key into ...\RunServices instead, and
indeed Xitami does then start up (although it shows an annoying "about"
screen wwhen so doing).

Then later, I saw that there IS a mention of running it as a Service
under Win9x, oddly enough on the downloads page (I didn't read any
further having once identified the package that I [thought] I wanted:-)

So today I fetched the console version, which has of course been updated
since my FTP session of last week, so I got bc3224d9.exe.  According to
the installation description "The Xitami console version installation
package asks whether you want to install it as a Win95 service".  SFAICS,
it did NOT ask this question; neither did it create "a small dispatcher,
called "C:\Services.bat" which simply changes to the Xitami directory and
then runs Xitami".

Has the installation procedure been botched since those words were
written?  Or has this part never been written after all?

Can I manually create the requisite batch file, and install the registry
key manually (I'm quite happy with registry hacking)?

As an extension, would it be possible to start the iASP admin and servlet
processes from within the same batch file as well?

Ah, but the thing is they've all _been_ retired, as of 6-12 months ago;
it's not like we've just decided to retire them now.

At the suggestion of one of our OS/2 users we've sent a "heads up" to
the makers of eComStation to see if they're interested in working with
us to keep Xitami binaries available for OS/2.  We'll see what comes of
that.

Meanwhile Xitami should build with gcc + EMX under OS/2 for anyone who
is interested in doing so.

And if we can find a spare machine and some spare time (!!) we'll try to
get an OS/2 build machine set up again.  Alas, spare time is in short
supply...

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jun  7 20:28:05 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dennis G. Wicks)
Date: Thu, 7 Jun 2001 12:28:05 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Setting Alias's
In-Reply-To: "Matt Jaworski" <jaworski@u.washington.edu>
 '[Xitami] Setting Alias's' (Jun  7, 10:00)
Message-ID: <200106071728.KAA26263@eskimo.com>

Matt,

You want something like this:

[Alias]
    Cd = "z:\\"
    Drv/a = "a:\\"
    Drv/c = "c:\\"
    Drv/d = "d:\\"
    Drv/e = "E:\\"
    Drv/f = "f:\\"
    Drv/g = "g:\\"
    Drv/x = "x:\\"
    Drv/y = "y:\\"
    Drv/z = "z:\\"

Hope this helps!

Good Luck!
Dennis

Date: Thu, 07 Jun 2001 18:38:12 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Domain Recognition
Message-ID: <001201c0efbb$afe7c9e0$b186fea9@gilberty>

Serious newbie question.  I have recently downloaded and installed Xitami's
webserver.  I have signed up for and received a personal domain.  I use
Windows ME for an OS.  I am hooked up to the internet via a DSL connection.
Now then, I have no idea in this world how to have Xitami recognize my
domain name.  Does it have to do with the network settings in my control
panel?  With my ISP?  With settings within Xitami?  What?

any and all help appreciated,
Dr. Gil


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 03:03:44 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jonathan Cilley)
Date: Thu, 7 Jun 2001 22:03:44 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Domain Recognition
In-Reply-To: <001201c0efbb$afe7c9e0$b186fea9@gilberty>
Message-ID: <NFBBJPBNELFPAPNEAKOOAEHCCCAA.jonathan@infoprimer.com>

Dr. Gil,

The First thing you will need to find out is if your DSL provider provides
you with a static or dynamic IP address. If you have a dynamic address, than
you will need to subscribe to a domain redirection service (bn3 is pretty
good). If you have a static IP address you have the option of running your
own DNS server (but with WinME stability could be an issue). If you choose
to run a DNS server, I suggest you buy a book on setting up a windows DNS
server as the process can be complicated and involve some steps that will
not be that easy for someone new to hosting web sites. Personally, if you
are new to this, I would go with a free redirection service like bn3 anyway,
especially if you have a static IP address. With bn3 you can redirect
http://www.yourdomain.com to your IP address and it will work great. If you
have a Dynamic IP address, you really don't have a choice other than to go
with a redirection service like bn3. If you would like to check out bn3's
offering go to http://www.bn3.com

Jonathan

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 08:39:25 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (GunnarSwan)
Date: 8 Jun 2001 00:39:25 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Domain Recognition
Message-ID: <20010608073925.10142.cpmta@c012.sfo.cp.net>

Where ever you got your domain name (www.MyName.com) .. they should have a facility to 
point to a DNS server. They may have their own DNS server IP's as default. I use my SDSL ISP domain.  
I paid for 8 static IP's.
At Register.Com (where I got my domain name), I point to my IP domain name server and I point my Static IP address on one of my boxes static IP here as my web site. 
The router assigns internal IP addresses, as does my ISP. The ISP maps Internal IP's to External IP's, so that TCP/IP can travel on a private network on my side of the firewall. (We have 3 pc's here).
The outside world can get to my machine by my desk via external IP address or domain name.
Do get a firewall; better to run NT. WinXX is unsafe in the real world. WinXX must be behind a firewall. It can't be in the DMZ or you may get hacked.
Get rid of Windows Networking. Only use TCP/IP. NT ships "Wide Open". NT must be locked down. Win98 is wide open and can't be locked down.  If this bumms you out, call M$.
There are some good books out there on NT and TCP/IP and Firewalls. Very interesting reading.
Good Luck. Hope This helps.

Many have answered the need to find your machine via the DNS with static ip's or another service.  I will just mention that I have a static ip and that the isp that registered my domains can point them to my static ip. (Yes thats right I point half a dozen at the same ip).  I then successfully use the virtual hosts in Xitami to pick up the domain name used in the url and serve up different web sites.  If anyone actually types in the numeric ip address then they get the default host pages.  It will work and Xitami has proved an excellant choice as I can now easily add my newly registered domains and have them all on the one server - even separtate log files to count the few people that visit !!!!

Yes I run it all on a Win98 pentium 160 box with 48MB ram and it stays up quite well on this platform.

Andy...

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 10:18:55 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 08 Jun 2001 21:18:55 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Setting Alias's
In-Reply-To: Message from david <webmaster@evernet.net>
 of "Thu, 07 Jun 2001 10:25:33 MST." <3B1FB90D.B1AC52B@evernet.net>
Message-ID: <200106080918.VAA22057@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3B1FB90D.B1AC52B@evernet.net>, david writes:
>:-) Very Small Error: Try this instead, notice the forward slash
>infront of "private"
> 
>[Alias]
>#   /private=e:\                         #   Directory/drive aliases
>#                                            #   E.g "http://xxxxx/mandy/"

I trust y'all realise that if you have a comment ("#") character at the
start, Xitami is going to ignore it as a comment?  You need something
like:

[Alias]
   /private=e:\

in order for Xitami to read it :-)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 12:19:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Fri, 08 Jun 2001 11:19:49 GMT
Subject: [Xitami] Running Xitami as a service under Win9x
Message-ID: <42167@dsl.co.uk>

In message <42119@dsl.co.uk>
   bhk@dsl.co.uk (Brian {Hamilton Kelly}) writes:

> Then later, I saw that there IS a mention of running it as a Service
> under Win9x, oddly enough on the downloads page (I didn't read any
> further having once identified the package that I [thought] I wanted:-)
> 
> So today I fetched the console version, which has of course been updated
> since my FTP session of last week, so I got bc3224d9.exe.  According to
> the installation description "The Xitami console version installation
> package asks whether you want to install it as a Win95 service".  SFAICS,
> it did NOT ask this question; neither did it create "a small dispatcher,
> called "C:\Services.bat" which simply changes to the Xitami directory and
> then runs Xitami".
> 
> Has the installation procedure been botched since those words were
> written?  Or has this part never been written after all?
> 
> Can I manually create the requisite batch file, and install the registry
> key manually (I'm quite happy with registry hacking)?

Sadly, I've seen no response to this query :-(

In the interim, I've written a batch file [C:\Xitami\Service.bat] of my
own, containing:
    C:
    cd \Xitami
    XiDOS32 -s
and have edited the relevant [...\RunServices] registry key to have an
additional entry:
    "Xitami" = "C:\Xitami\Service.bat"

This works OK originally: the HTTP server starts running about the same
time as the "Login to Domain" dialogue box appears on the screen.  (I had
to edit the job's properties so that it started minimized, rather than
having a blobby-great DOS-box on the screen.)

The service continues to work happily also after a user has logged in for
the first time.  However, when that user elects to "Start -> Shutdown ->
Close all programs and log in as a different user" then the server
process also gets killed.

This isn't really very useful; surely after having been started with the
-s switch[1] the process ought not to be a candidate for killing off on
user "logout"?

I'm suspecting that we shall have to revert to the bw (Windows version)
and just be content with its being started through the Run key for each
login, and then not have the user logout.

> As an extension, would it be possible to start the iASP admin and servlet

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 11:55:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 08 Jun 2001 22:55:21 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Running Xitami as a service under Win9x
In-Reply-To: Message from bhk@dsl.co.uk (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
 of "Fri, 08 Jun 2001 11:19:49 GMT." <42167@dsl.co.uk>
Message-ID: <200106081055.WAA24910@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <42167@dsl.co.uk>, Brian {Hamilton Kelly} writes:
>In message <42119@dsl.co.uk>
>   bhk@dsl.co.uk (Brian {Hamilton Kelly}) writes:
>> Then later, I saw that there IS a mention of running it as a Service
>> under Win9x, oddly enough on the downloads page (I didn't read any
>> further having once identified the package that I [thought] I wanted:-)
>> [....]
>> Has the installation procedure been botched since those words were
>> written?  Or has this part never been written after all?
>
>Sadly, I've seen no response to this query :-(

This is largely because no one knows the answer :-)  Windows 95/98
really are not intended for running services on them; any attempts to do
otherwise are at best somewhat hopeful and as you have found.

Basically from what I've been able to find out any "services" you run
under Windows 95 generally start when you log in, and stop when you log
out, and there's relatively little you can do about that.  Apparently if
you install the NT Service version (bs3224d9.exe) under Windows 95 it
will register itself in basically the way that you have found.

Alternatively you can run the DOS console version in a minimised window
as you have done (the "-s" switch doesn't do anything under DOS/Windows
other than print out the message you saw; it does useful things only in
Unix and OS/2).  However as you've found, it'll be stopped when the user
logs out.

Basically if you'll need to choose between: (a) having Xitami running
when a user is logged in, on a user workstation OS like Windows 95/98,
and (b) running Xitami on a more server oriented OS (Linux, Unix,
Windows NT/2000, even OS/2).

Sorry about that.  But unfortunately it's inherient in the way that
Windows 95/98 works: it's not intended to run "services" in the way
server OSes are, and Microsoft went to some lengths to make it more
difficult.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 15:00:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 09 Jun 2001 02:00:33 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] admin problem
In-Reply-To: Message from tom mcpharlin <mcpharln@pacbell.net>
 of "Fri, 02 Feb 2001 01:22:08 CDT." <3A7A515A.9020500@pacbell.net>
Message-ID: <200106081400.CAA26869@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3A7A515A.9020500@pacbell.net>, tom mcpharlin writes:
>I'm running Xitami 2.4.d7 on a windows 2000 system. When I try to access 
>the admin page, I enter the name/password in defaults.aut and then get 
>the message:
>"The function you requested is not implemented"

As far as I can remember this message will appear only if Xitami detects
the path as a WSX (web server extension, like the admin pages), but 
then cannot find the extension that is supposed to be there (eg, because
the name is wrong).

The [Wsx] section of the config file specifies that "admin" should be
handled by "xiadmin"; if you've changed your config files (eg,
defaults.cfg, etc) for some reason so that "admin" points at another
name that might cause the problem.  So perhaps check carefully through
your defaults.cfg file.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>section:

The 501 (not implemented) error message indicates that there is no
"xisetup" that can be run.  AFAICT this is because there is no
"xisetup"; the web based admin is "xiadmin", usually at "/admin", and is
set up by the default configuration.

You can set up virtual hosts through the web based admin (at /admin).

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 15:51:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 09 Jun 2001 02:51:12 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] problems with vhosts
In-Reply-To: Message from "bernd hohmann" <hohmann@conacom.de>
 of "Thu, 14 Sep 2000 10:09:00 EST." <200009141008.5852921.6@ec-computers.net>
Message-ID: <200106081451.CAA28070@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <200009141008.5852921.6@ec-computers.net>, "bernd hohmann" writes:
>defined default security:
>   admin=0
>   [/admin]
>     {empty}
>
>BERND security
>   admin=1
>   [/admin]
>     berndadmin=berndadmin
>[....]
>this should disallow the admin-function when browsing the default-host but 
>allow it when using host BERND.

The issue here is that the [security] admin=N setting controls whether
the admin section is even started up, as Xitami starts.  At this point
only the main configuration file (xitami.cfg, defaults.cfg) is
available, and hence the setting is a global setting.  If you disable it
in the main file, then the admin section is never started, so will not
be available under a virtual host or anywhere basically.

As far as I can tell the [security] admin=N setting in the virtual hosts
is never even tested.

What you could possibly do (you'll need to test this with your setup),
is use the [wsx] admin=... settings in the virtual hosts where you don't
want the admin available, to override what the /admin path maps to.
This should cause "the function you requested is not implemented" for
thos virtual hosts.  Providing it does, you can then take the password
section out for /admin for those virtual hosts, and anyone trying will
immediately get that error message.  Then on the virtual host where you
do wish to access the admin, you can use the password section, and not
override the [wsx] admin=.... setting, and it should, in theory, work
there.

Possibly the documentation should be clearer as to what settings are
global and what are per-virtual-host.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 19:19:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 08 Jun 2001 14:19:12 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Domain Recognition
References: <001201c0efbb$afe7c9e0$b186fea9@gilberty>
Message-ID: <3B211720.639E4B35@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  how to have Xitami recognize my domain name. 

Web servers don't know their own names. (They can, but they don't have to.)

And there are really no names on the Internet, only numbers.

But people prefer to give machines names, because numbers are hard to
remember.

Look at what happens when you type a name like "yahoo.com" at your browser.
The browser says "What do I do with this? I need a number!". But it knows that
the user probably does not know the number. 

What the webserver (actually the TCP network stack) does is ask a DNS server.
All ISPs are required to have a DNS server to serve their customers and to
answer requests for name/number lookups from other DNS servers.

I have a site http://summerfest.rutgers.edu . You are using pbi.net (PacBell?)
as an ISP. Your browser calls pbi.net's DNS server and asks "What's the number
for summerfest.rutgers.edu?" pbi.net's DNS server probably never heard of
summerfest.rutgers.edu, but it heard of rutgers.edu (or it asks a master .EDU
DNS system for the number of rutgers.edu's DNS server). It asks
DNS1.rutgers.edu "what is the number for summerfest.rutgers.edu?" and gets the
answer "165.230.87.130". Your browser opens 165.230.87.130. The Xitami at that
address serves you a page. 

Now, how did DNS1.rutgers.edu know that summerfest.rutgers.edu is a name for
165.230.87.130 ? I called our DNS guy and asked him to add
"summerfest.rutgers.edu", pointed to that IP number, to Rutgers' DNS system. 

Since you have a Commercial ISP, there will be differences. First: is your IP
number Static? My server's IP number has never changed. Many DSL etc accounts
get a new IP number every few days. There are ways to handle Dynamic IP
allocation, but it is trickier and less reliable than a Static IP. Note that
asking your ISP for a Static IP may require that you convert to a more
expensive "business" account!

With a static IP, your ISP should be able to add your hostname to their DNS
system, for all the world to lookup. But at Commercial ISP providers, this
often costs "extra".

And by asking for a Static IP and a DNS entry, you are telling your ISP that
you are running a public server. Such servers -sometimes- generate a lot of
traffic, more than the ISP expects for a "home surfer" account. So they may
bump you up to a more expensive account. 

Technically you can buy DNS service from anyone. There are even "Dynamic IP
DNS" servers that can change your listed IP number almost as often as your ISP
reassigns your IP number. 

You "can" set up your own DNS service, but: (A) this is very geeky stuff to do
correctly (B) some -other- DNS service has to know about your DNS service or
nobody will find your DNS server. You can register your own DNS with InterNIC
(the people who hold your domain name registration) but they like to see two
DNS providers, not in the same place. I don't think this is for a "serious
newbie" as you describe yourself. 

The "right" answer is "Call your ISP and talk". But try to avoid saying who
you are until you find out if this will run up your bill. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 20:34:08 2001

FWIW, a colleague of mine tried installing Xitami on some machines in a
teaching lab last year (I don't know which version he was using).  The
machines all worked fine if one logged in to them as "admin", or with
otherwise unrestricted accounts, yet if one logged in with a very
restricted account[1], the server would only respond to the loopback
address, and not to that of the LAN[2].

I'm pleased to say that bw3224b9 does *not* suffer with this problem: it
runs with both the 127.0.0.1 and the allocated 193.63.241.* addresses
quite happily whatever the privileges of the user account.

[1] I've used the System Policy Editor[3] to create very restrictive
accounts to prevent students screwing up the configurations of these
Win95 machines; it works *really* well.  (Of course, it makes it much
easier to prevent these policies being circumvented by having a PDC on
the network too.)

[2] The LAN has fixed, pre-allocated IP addresses: no DHCP involved here.

[3] There have been no changes to the policies between last year's
failures and this year's successes: originally, I had thought that some
part of a policy prevented a server process from binding to, and/or
listening on, any IP address other than 127.0.0.1.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun  8 21:02:22 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Fri, 08 Jun 2001 20:02:22 GMT
Subject: [Xitami] Running Xitami as a service under Win9x
Message-ID: <42203@dsl.co.uk>

In message <200106081055.WAA24910@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>
   Ewen McNeill writes:

> This is largely because no one knows the answer :-)  Windows 95/98
> really are not intended for running services on them; any attempts to do
> otherwise are at best somewhat hopeful and as you have found.
> 
> Basically from what I've been able to find out any "services" you run
> under Windows 95 generally start when you log in, and stop when you log
> out, and there's relatively little you can do about that.  Apparently if
> you install the NT Service version (bs3224d9.exe) under Windows 95 it
> will register itself in basically the way that you have found.

If something is place in the registry key
[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run], then
it will be executed (asynchronously) when anyone logs in.  If placed in
the [...\RunServices] key, then it will be executed when Windows first
boots up.  (I make use of the RunServiceOnce key to execute some commands
that configure each machine in the lab, when they've all been downloaded
an identical Ghosted image: works brilliantly.)

What I hadn't appreciated was that something started from the RunServices
key is killed off, like any other program, when a user logs out.  And
there is then no mechanism by which it will be restarted on the next log
in.

Daft, in my book.

> Alternatively you can run the DOS console version in a minimised window
> as you have done (the "-s" switch doesn't do anything under DOS/Windows
> other than print out the message you saw; it does useful things only in
> Unix and OS/2).  However as you've found, it'll be stopped when the user
> logs out.

Indeed :-(

I have now reverted to running the Win32 version rather than the console
one, and it's fired up when someone logs in.

Incidentally, and this is the main point of this posting, I found that
the file bw3224d9.exe on the Belgian mirror site is corrupted.  Instead
of transferring 700kB, it stops after 68kB (and obviously the resultant

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jun 10 13:54:48 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 11 Jun 2001 00:54:48 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami 2.4d9/Xitami 2.5b5
In-Reply-To: Message from "Dr. Martin R. Hadam" <Hadam.Martin@mh-hannover.de>
 of "Fri, 08 Jun 2001 21:40:29 +0100." <E158S7R-0000Ee-00@Mail.MH-Hannover.DE>
Message-ID: <200106101254.AAA26847@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <E158S7R-0000Ee-00@Mail.MH-Hannover.DE>, "Dr. Martin R. Hadam" writes:
> I've been moving machines and today, Xitami provided some message, for
>the first time:
>2001/06/08 21:32:16: smthttp: HTTP service is now running
>Fatal error in application - aborted
>Abort at smtsock:Check-For-Expired-Requests: (Getting-Event, Empty-Event)
>Abnormal program termination

Ah, that sort of problem.  You might want to keep an eye on whether it's
always at the same point, or whether the problems shift around.  If they
shift around it's most likely that something is writing to memory it
shouldn't.  If it's always (or usually) one place, then possibly there's
something wrong with the way that some requests are handled by smtsock.

Unfortunately either way they're difficult to diagnose problems, since
they're not easily reproducable.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Does this ONLY occur in directory listings via aliases?  Or does it
occur with any directory listing?  My guess is that it would occur with
any directory listing generated by Xitami, and I suspect it is related
to the URL-encoding being done by Xitami.  You can perhaps work around
this issue in httpdir.gsl (in the templates directory), by using "name"
rather than "nameurl" in the links. (This will cause some other problems
though, especially with names with spaces in them.)

If it does occur in all listings it is already on our bug list.  If it
occurs ONLY in directory listings via aliases we'll need to narrow down
what is special about the directory listings via aliases so we can add
it as a new bug.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jun 10 16:37:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 11 Jun 2001 03:37:49 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] directory listings
In-Reply-To: Message from Mike Shumko <mike.shumko@robelle.com>
 of "Mon, 05 Mar 2001 12:36:57 CDT." <2D123C9B36C5D31182B90090279CF9A6295F04@CLIFFY>
Message-ID: <200106101537.DAA28480@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <2D123C9B36C5D31182B90090279CF9A6295F04@CLIFFY>, Mike Shumko writes:
>I am using Xitami 2.4d7 on WinNT, the 'service' version.
>I do not want Xitami to produce a directory listing when there is no default
>web document present in a given directory. The dirlist switch does not seem
>to work for suppressing these listings. That is, regardless of whether I
>enable or disable it, listings are always produced. 

The dirlist option appears to operate correctly with 2.4d9 under Linux;
if set to "1" then directory listings are allowed, if set to "0" then a
forbidden message is generated.

Beware that there are two dirlist options; one for the CGI directory and
one for the overall server security.  The one you want to disable all
directory listings is:

[Security]
  dirlist=0

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jun 10 16:41:08 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 11 Jun 2001 03:41:08 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami serving JSP
In-Reply-To: Message from "Tim Fiddimore" <tsf@posford-ln.co.uk>
 of "Mon, 05 Mar 2001 04:39:01 CDT." <3AA35E12.23619.E70D5C0@localhost>
Message-ID: <200106101541.DAA28526@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3AA35E12.23619.E70D5C0@localhost>, "Tim Fiddimore" writes:
>What I want to do is pass the JSP file directly to the servlet, so I 
>can use a url of the form:-
>
>http://mydomain/examples/example.jsp
>
>I cant seem to find any way of associating JSP files with the servlet.

The main issue here is that the ServletRunner has no syntax for saying
to Xitami "give me all the files ending in this extension".  In theory
(I haven't tried this) if you can get the LRWP request to be for ".jsp"
then all ".jsp" files should be passed to that LRWP (and with the way
the ServletRunner works, to that servlet).

So if you are up to a bit of Java programming you might be able to hack
the ServletRunner to pass the ".jsp" string across for the servlet that
is handling the JSP files in its (or one of its) LRWP registrations.

Really what is needed is some sort of config file syntax for specifying
this, but that may have to wait until I can merge in the changes to the
ServletRunner that a user sent in.  (Ie, more spare time :-) )

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jun 10 16:47:20 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 11 Jun 2001 03:47:20 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] SSI
In-Reply-To: Message from Ben Franske <autosort@subdimension.com>
 of "Tue, 16 Jan 2001 21:06:19 CDT." <5.0.2.1.2.20010116193518.00aae5f0@pop-server>
Message-ID: <200106101547.DAA28754@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <5.0.2.1.2.20010116193518.00aae5f0@pop-server>, Ben Franske writes:
>I'm having a problem with SSI in Xitami. This is in a virtual host the 
>error message I get is "The function you requested is not implemented" The 
>SSI code is <!--#include virtual="/news/news.txt" --> and it is on a 
>virtual host with a config file like this:

"The function you requested is not implemented" is usually generated
when you refer to a WSX which is not compiled into Xitami.  In this case
you are explicitly setting WSX references for xixssi, which shouldn't
normally be required (they are in xitami.cfg for the versions have
xixssi):

>[Wsx]
>     .shtml=xixssi
>     .ssi=xixssi

You don't say what version of Xitami you are using.  If you are using
Xitami 2.4 you need to use perlssi (as a filter, it should be
preconfigured in the default configuration).  If you are using Xitami
2.5, then xixssi should be installed and set up automatically, in which
case you don't need those [wsx] entries.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jun 10 19:18:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

> restrict the cgi-bin from viewing but can still use it to run cgi's and pl programs?

In 2.4, the contents of cgi-bin are not directly visible, only
their output is served, as long as you use the default location
(NOT under the webpages directory) and don't set any aliases to
it. 

Don't set "Allow file mixing?" in the CGI settings, if you can
possibly help it.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jun 11 21:10:29 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 11 Jun 2001 16:10:29 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] running server on RAM drive
References: <200106091158.XAA03312@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz> <03c001c0f2b0$8dfb0ca0$a600a8c0@Michael>
Message-ID: <3B2525B5.1F20B7E1@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I've setup RAM drive recently, and consider putting web server pages on it
to speed up access a bit. Is it worth it ...?

My guesses are:

Most current hard drives are faster than any network that carries other
traffic,

Disk-cache in Windows (and surely unix) will quickly fill with the most-used
files and deliver them at RAM speed. This is a very real effect, I discovered
years ago in DOS when I maxed-out the disk cache. After the first time I
accessed a file, the next time(s) it loaded as if from RAM drive, unless I had
opened more than 8 megs (SmartDrv's limit) of files in the meantime.
 
I think your RAM drive is just taking RAM away from Windows' disk cache. And
Windows' disk cache actually works well, and is probably at least as fast as
the antique code in RAMdrive.

I could see a RAM drive in the case where you have rarely used files that MUST
load quickly. Being rarely used, they will fall out of disk cache between
uses. But with the relative speeds of modern drives and the typical congested
network link, you may not be able to see the difference at the browser.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jun 11 22:21:32 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael S. Kazarin)
Date: Tue, 12 Jun 2001 01:21:32 +0400
Subject: [Xitami] running server on RAM drive
References: <200106091158.XAA03312@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz> <03c001c0f2b0$8dfb0ca0$a600a8c0@Michael> <3B2525B5.1F20B7E1@rci.rutgers.edu>
Message-ID: <03ca01c0f2bc$7eea1f60$a600a8c0@Michael>

Actually, the RAM drive resides in non-paged memory pool, therefore the data
it holds is never written to disk except changes to data if any are written
on an hourly schedule.

| My guesses are:
|
| Most current hard drives are faster than any network that carries other
| traffic,
|
| Disk-cache in Windows (and surely unix) will quickly fill with the
most-used
| files and deliver them at RAM speed. This is a very real effect, I
discovered
| years ago in DOS when I maxed-out the disk cache. After the first time I
| accessed a file, the next time(s) it loaded as if from RAM drive, unless I
had
| opened more than 8 megs (SmartDrv's limit) of files in the meantime.
|
| I think your RAM drive is just taking RAM away from Windows' disk cache.
And
| Windows' disk cache actually works well, and is probably at least as fast
as
| the antique code in RAMdrive.
|
| I could see a RAM drive in the case where you have rarely used files that
MUST
| load quickly. Being rarely used, they will fall out of disk cache between
| uses. But with the relative speeds of modern drives and the typical
congested
| network link, you may not be able to see the difference at the browser.
|
|  -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 12 09:26:12 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 12 Jun 2001 20:26:12 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] running server on RAM drive
In-Reply-To: Message from "Michael S. Kazarin" <kazarin@eltra.metrocom.ru>
 of "Mon, 11 Jun 2001 23:56:03 +0400." <03c001c0f2b0$8dfb0ca0$a600a8c0@Michael>
Message-ID: <200106120826.UAA12952@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <03c001c0f2b0$8dfb0ca0$a600a8c0@Michael>, "Michael S. Kazarin" writes:
>I'm running Xitami 2.5b5 on w2k sp2.
>I've setup RAM drive recently, and consider putting web server pages on it
>to speed up access a bit. Is it worth it and are there any limitations?

The main limitation is that obviously you can't keep the master copy of
things on your ram drive, as it will go away when you reboot :-)  Which
means you've got to handle copying things into the ram drive on startup,
and making sure you copy anything you want to keep off before you reboot
(which is a pain if you are forced to reboot without shutting down
cleanly).

As to whether it is worth it, that is a much harder question these days:
modern OS (and W2K is modern enough for this purpose) cache things that
have been read from the disk pretty well.  So that things which are
being used are kept in memory (in the disk cache) even if their
permanent home is on a real disk.

So basically a ram disk is betting that you know better than the OS what
is being used a lot: it certainly used to be true with DOS, but it's
far less true with a modern OS.  Usually the ram is better just left for
the OS to use for caching; but experiment and see what you think.
Remember that ram you take for the ram drive won't be available for
running programs; which if you have limited ram can force the machine to
swap, which is rather... bad.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 12 09:43:00 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 12 Jun 2001 20:43:00 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] virtual hosts / multiple cgi-bin
In-Reply-To: Message from "hank doe" <hankdoe@hotmail.com>
 of "Tue, 12 Jun 2001 10:12:53 +0430." <F133rIkyPzGNsokLQ8a0000e0d9@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <200106120843.UAA14202@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <F133rIkyPzGNsokLQ8a0000e0d9@hotmail.com>, "hank doe" writes:
>http://www.dummy.com/users/<username>/.....
>
>i've got 2 problems now. the first one is about cgi's.
>1) how do i setup cgi-dirs for every of those users ?

Set the "cgi anywhere" flag (beware, this is a security risk if you let
people upload their own content: they can upload and run any program
they like on your system).  [CGI] wildcard=1 controls this.

>the 2nd) (i suppose this is the more elegant way)
>can i achieve the same with virtual hosts ? and how to setup them,
>probably there is an idiot proof instruction manual ? :-)

If you can live with urls like:

http://username.example.com/

then you can give each a virtual host.  You can set these up in the
virtual host portion of the web based admin -- and once you've got the
config files for one you'll probably find you can easily replicate them
by copying an existing one and changing the names.  With the virtual
host approach you can give each their own cgi-bin directory, and
webpages directory and so on.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 12 13:46:16 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Craig Morrison)

Subject: [Xitami] running server on RAM drive
References: <200106120826.UAA12952@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>
Message-ID: <3B260F18.2A379E40@2cah.com>

To go along with this line of thinking..

The non-paged memory pool on Win32 platforms is *not* something you want to
run short of. In an earlier message it was stated that the RAM disk was held
in this memory pool. Bad idea, on a high-load server, if this pool runs short
your machine will crash and die a horrible death.

Ewen McNeill wrote:
> 
> So basically a ram disk is betting that you know better than the OS what
> is being used a lot: it certainly used to be true with DOS, but it's
> far less true with a modern OS.  Usually the ram is better just left for
> the OS to use for caching; but experiment and see what you think.
> Remember that ram you take for the ram drive won't be available for
> running programs; which if you have limited ram can force the machine to
> swap, which is rather... bad.

Hmmm... I don't think I even addressed the issue of writing. 

>  changes to data if any are written on an hourly schedule.

And certainly I'm sure you know that a RAM drive doesn't copy to disk by
itself, so I guess you'll be using a timer and script to handle that bit. 

I used RAM drives a LOT, back in MFM days when hard drives were slightly
faster than a telegraph. I'm aware that they are still useful stages for
program compilation, where there is much disk work but only the final result
has to be saved. 

But on a web server, my guess is that disk speed is almost never a limit.

Try it and let us know.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 12 16:25:45 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

References: <F133rIkyPzGNsokLQ8a0000e0d9@hotmail.com>

> can i achieve the same with virtual hosts ? 

What Ewen says.

Note that this requires additional DNS entries, whereas
www.dummy.com/JohnSmith/ only requires that www.dummy.com be registered in
DNS.   
If you manage your own DNS, no problem. And the username entries can be CNAME
pointers to the one IP entry.

If you buy DNS service from somewhere else, adding hostnames to DNS may cost
you money.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun 13 10:19:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 13 Jun 2001 21:19:21 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Access Log
In-Reply-To: Message from "Paul Richards" <grangeway@btinternet.com>
 of "Wed, 13 Jun 2001 03:15:55 +0100." <MAEPKOFMKPDCFOHCHFAFKEJACMAA.grangeway@btinternet.com>
Message-ID: <200106130919.VAA27186@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <MAEPKOFMKPDCFOHCHFAFKEJACMAA.grangeway@btinternet.com>, "Paul Richards" writes:
>>62.42.174.237 - anonymous [08/Jun/2001:17:12:27 -0500]
>>"ftp://62.42.174.237/C:\WINDOWS\TEMP\./ls000001.ftp" 226 -1
>
>The 4th string appears to be what the ftp service logs in xitami when a user
>issues an "ls" command. 

Yes, that's correct.  As far as I can tell what gets logged is:

ftp://YOURIPADDRESS/TEMPDIRNAME/TEMPFILENAME

wher YOURIPADDRESS is the IP address they FTP'd to; TEMPDIRNAME is
whatever name you've told Xitami to use for temporary files (by default
it is "temp" which uses the value of the TEMP environment variable if
set), and TEMPFILENAME is the temporary file Xitami creates with the
directory listing in it prior to sending it.

>This seems like a confusing way to log this? ewen?

The difficulty is that Xitami tries to log these in the same log as the
HTTP requests, and hence needs to make them "distinct" in some way.  And
"ls" type requests don't transfer a real file.

Suggestions for alternatives welcomed.  Maybe it has to be a separate log?

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun 13 16:49:44 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 14 Jun 2001 03:49:44 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Setting Alias's
In-Reply-To: Message from "Matt Jaworski" <jaworski@u.washington.edu>
 of "Wed, 13 Jun 2001 08:27:40 MST." <005701c0f41d$61f72670$a65c5f80@neelix>
Message-ID: <200106131549.DAA30309@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <005701c0f41d$61f72670$a65c5f80@neelix>, "Matt Jaworski" writes:
>How do I link up the info in another drive?

Create an alias that points at that other drive (or preferably a
directory on it), eg:

[Alias]
   mydir=d:\mydir

Then you can use URLs like:

http://www.example.com/mydir/myfile.html

You can't use drive letters directly in URLs.  (And even indirectly you
can use them only in file:/// URLs which work ONLY on your local PC.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

> This is what I discovered:
> 
> 1) Halcyonsoft Instant ASP (iASP) works with Xitami
> and MS Access 2000 (which requires ASP) - read this on
> iASP's forum.  BUTTTTTTT ... I can't find where to
> download a free version of iASP (i saw free version of
> iASP on the net (version 1.08 at cnet.download.com)
> but no longer downloadable!

I downloaded it (for work) from www.halcyonsoft.com; look for their
"Developer's Edition" which is a 9MB self-installing EXE file.  Only
permits ten concurrent connections.

I am having some problems with this, and am in e-mail dialogue with one
of Halcyon's people.  If anyone else *here* has experience of using iASP
with Xitami under Windoze (I'm using 2.4d9 on Win95C), I'm sure it would
be of interest to Ethereal Being and myself.

(In particular, the two "problems" I've found to date are:
    1) iASP doesn't provide a Content-Length HTTP header on the documents
    it serves up (even if they actually have no dynamic content at all,
    but just happen to have the .asp extension).  This results in the
    client (ie the browser) sitting there awaiting further data, until
    either it or the Xitami server decide to expire a timeout and close
    the TCP/IP channel
    2) I've been unable to instantiate a VBscript object of the RegExp
    class; e.g.
        dim reg
        set reg = new RegExp
    iASP (or something) barfs on the latter, and instead of returning the
    expected HTML, gives a message about being unable to create an
    ActiveX object.
Has anyone else had these, or similar, experiences with iASP?)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jun 14 08:36:20 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael S. Kazarin)
Date: Thu, 14 Jun 2001 11:36:20 +0400
Subject: [Xitami] Running Xitami as a service under Win9x
References: <200106081055.WAA24910@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>
Message-ID: <002301c0f4a4$b6338ee0$659305c3@futures>

Hi!

Perhaps that info can help:

Before I started exploring Xitami on w2k I used to run GUI version of Xitami
on Win9x,ME (xiwin32.exe). There is the way to start Xitami at pre-login as
a service.
You simply hack a registry a bit. Go to
HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows\Current Version\RunServices. Create new
REG_SZ there. Moify it to contain C:\Xitami\xiwin32.exe (or whatever your
path will be). Bingo. Now your Xitami will start early before anyone logs in
and stay running after logout till you shut down.
Limitations: you will have no tray icon, you'll have to ctrl-alt-del/end
task the server if you wish to stop or restart (except wba) the server.

Mike.


| This is largely because no one knows the answer :-)  Windows 95/98
| really are not intended for running services on them; any attempts to do
| otherwise are at best somewhat hopeful and as you have found.
|
| Basically from what I've been able to find out any "services" you run
| under Windows 95 generally start when you log in, and stop when you log
| out, and there's relatively little you can do about that.  Apparently if
| you install the NT Service version (bs3224d9.exe) under Windows 95 it
| will register itself in basically the way that you have found.
|
| Alternatively you can run the DOS console version in a minimised window
| as you have done (the "-s" switch doesn't do anything under DOS/Windows
| other than print out the message you saw; it does useful things only in
| Unix and OS/2).  However as you've found, it'll be stopped when the user
| logs out.
|
| Basically if you'll need to choose between: (a) having Xitami running
| when a user is logged in, on a user workstation OS like Windows 95/98,
| and (b) running Xitami on a more server oriented OS (Linux, Unix,
| Windows NT/2000, even OS/2).
|
| Sorry about that.  But unfortunately it's inherient in the way that
| Windows 95/98 works: it's not intended to run "services" in the way
| server OSes are, and Microsoft went to some lengths to make it more
| difficult.
|
| Ewen
|
| --
| Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com
|
| --
| Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
| To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami
|

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jun 14 12:20:11 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 14 Jun 2001 23:20:11 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] xitami and other web servers
In-Reply-To: Message from "garry" <garry@cable.net.nz>
 of "Thu, 14 Jun 2001 22:04:34 +1200." <001101c0f4b9$69b80a90$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>
Message-ID: <200106141120.XAA06549@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <001101c0f4b9$69b80a90$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>, "garry" writes:
>Hi i have used xitami for many years and am happy with it
>my question is how do you run say apache beside xitami and have the right
>server pick up when the request is to a domain hosted on it ?

I'm assuming that you want to run both on the same server, and both
without any special port numbers, in which case your choices are:

(a) run them on different IP addresses, and have the DNS for those
domains point at the appropriate IP address.

(b) have one server forward requests for some domains to the other
server (Apache can do this with mod_proxy; Xitami needs some sort of
add-on, perhaps a LRWP program, to do this).

Of these (a) is somewhat easier to handle, but (b) will work just fine.
However if your reason for running Xitami is to handle "simple" requests
without bothering Apache, then (b) might not be such a good solution.

For just testing, simply running them on different ports is often the
easiest solution.  (Both Xitami and Apache can be told to use different
ports.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

In-Reply-To: Message from "Thomas J. Hruska" <shinelight@crosswinds.net>
 of "Thu, 14 Jun 2001 10:20:26 EST." <3.0.6.32.20010614102026.007a39b0@pop.crosswinds.net>
Message-ID: <200106141551.DAA08751@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3.0.6.32.20010614102026.007a39b0@pop.crosswinds.net>, "Thomas J. Hru
ska" writes:
>From: <http://lists.xitami.org/pipermail/xitami/>
>
>There is a link to:
><http://lists.xitami.org/pipermail/xitami/2001-May/thread.html>
>
>Which returns the happy HTTP/404 Error.

Congratulations, you have found a bug in Xitami :-)

What seems to be happening is that Xitami was lower casing the URL
somewhere along the way, but since this server is running on Linux, when
it does that with paths that are actually in upper case, it can no
longer access the directories: hence 404.

I've worked around this temporarily (symbolic links), which will last
until the end of the month (I hope), and obviously we'll put this bug
onto our bug list :-)

Thanks for chasing this up.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

XiFusion v2.5 (a link to it is now available from the Xitami add-ons page)
will solve your problem.  It will handle both relative and absolute page
redirection (the latter is sent back to the browser for processing and
forwarding).  While XiFusion v2.5 is designed primarily for interfacing
ColdFusion with Xitami, it provides an excellent wrapper for PHP (v4.x) as
well.

ites:
>Had a few crashes with 2.4d9, so I thought I'd drop a quick note here to see
>if anyone else had any problems:

>Error message was:
>  Assertion Failed!
>  Module c:\work\imatix\release\xitami-24\src\smt\smtlib.c, line 1309

That assertion checks that when the internal routines are trying to
locate an internal method call, both the name of the "agent" (FTP, HTTP,
etc), and the name of the method are defined.  Since these should always
be defined, I'm puzzled as to why you are receiving the messages you
are.

Do they happen after anything in particular has occured?  Have you found
a way to repeat them?  Being able to reproduce a problem like this is
the biggest step to solving it.

**** Help for Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:


This help message is being sent to you from the Majordomo mailing list
management system at Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.

This is version 1.94.5 of Majordomo.

If you're familiar with mail servers, an advanced user's summary of
Majordomo's commands appears at the end of this message.

Majordomo is an automated system which allows users to subscribe
and unsubscribe to mailing lists, and to retrieve files from list
archives.

You can interact with the Majordomo software by sending it commands
in the body of mail messages addressed to "Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
".
Please do not put your commands on the subject line; Majordomo does
not process commands in the subject line.

You may put multiple Majordomo commands in the same mail message.
Put each command on a line by itself.

If you use a "signature block" at the end of your mail, Majordomo may
mistakenly believe each line of your message is a command; you will
then receive spurious error messages.  To keep this from happening,
either put a line starting with a hyphen ("-") before your signature,
or put a line with just the word

	end

on it in the same place.  This will stop the Majordomo software from
processing your signature as bad commands.

Here are some of the things you can do using Majordomo:

I.	FINDING OUT WHICH LISTS ARE ON THIS SYSTEM

To get a list of publicly-available mailing lists on this system, put the
following line in the body of your mail message to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	lists

Each line will contain the name of a mailing list and a brief description
of the list.

To get more information about a particular list, use the "info" command,
supplying the name of the list.  For example, if the name of the list 
about which you wish information is "demo-list", you would put the line

	info demo-list

in the body of the mail message.

II.	SUBSCRIBING TO A LIST

Once you've determined that you wish to subscribe to one or more lists on
this system, you can send commands to Majordomo to have it add you to the
list, so you can begin receiving mailings.

To receive list mail at the address from which you're sending your mail,
simply say "subscribe" followed by the list's name:

	subscribe demo-list

If for some reason you wish to have the mailings go to a different address
(a friend's address, a specific other system on which you have an account,
or an address which is more correct than the one that automatically appears 
in the "From:" header on the mail you send), you would add that address to
the command.  For instance, if you're sending a request from your work
account, but wish to receive "demo-list" mail at your personal account
(for which we will use "jqpublic@my-isp.com" as an example), you'd put
the line

	subscribe demo-list jqpublic@my-isp.com

in the mail message body.

Based on configuration decisions made by the list owners, you may be added 
to the mailing list automatically.  You may also receive notification
that an authorization key is required for subscription.  Another message
will be sent to the address to be subscribed (which may or may not be the
same as yours) containing the key, and directing the user to send a
command found in that message back to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.  (This can be
a bit of extra hassle, but it helps keep you from being swamped in extra
email by someone who forged requests from your address.)  You may also
get a message that your subscription is being forwarded to the list owner
for approval; some lists have waiting lists, or policies about who may
subscribe.  If your request is forwarded for approval, the list owner
should contact you soon after your request.

Upon subscribing, you should receive an introductory message, containing
list policies and features.  Save this message for future reference; it
will also contain exact directions for unsubscribing.  If you lose the
intro mail and would like another copy of the policies, send this message
to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	intro demo-list

(substituting, of course, the real name of your list for "demo-list").

III.	UNSUBSCRIBING FROM MAILING LISTS

Your original intro message contains the exact command which should be
used to remove your address from the list.  However, in most cases, you
may simply send the command "unsubscribe" followed by the list name:

	unsubscribe demo-list

(This command may fail if your provider has changed the way your
address is shown in your mail.)

To remove an address other than the one from which you're sending
the request, give that address in the command:

	unsubscribe demo-list jqpublic@my-isp.com

In either of these cases, you can tell Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
 to remove
the address in question from all lists on this server by using "*"
in place of the list name:

	unsubscribe *
	unsubscribe * jqpublic@my-isp.com

IV.	FINDING THE LISTS TO WHICH AN ADDRESS IS SUBSCRIBED

To find the lists to which your address is subscribed, send this command
in the body of a mail message to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	which

You can look for other addresses, or parts of an address, by specifying
the text for which Majordomo should search.  For instance, to find which
users at my-isp.com are subscribed to which lists, you might send the
command

	which my-isp.com

Note that many list owners completely or fully disable the "which"
command, considering it a privacy violation.

V.	FINDING OUT WHO'S SUBSCRIBED TO A LIST

To get a list of the addresses on a particular list, you may use the
"who" command, followed by the name of the list:

	who demo-list

Note that many list owners allow only a list's subscribers to use the
"who" command, or disable it completely, believing it to be a privacy
violation.

VI.	RETRIEVING FILES FROM A LIST'S ARCHIVES

Many list owners keep archives of files associated with a list.  These
may include:
- back issues of the list
- help files, user profiles, and other documents associated with the list
- daily, monthly, or yearly archives for the list

To find out if a list has any files associated with it, use the "index"
command:

	index demo-list

If you see files in which you're interested, you may retrieve them by
using the "get" command and specifying the list name and archive filename.
For instance, to retrieve the files called "profile.form" (presumably a
form to fill out with your profile) and "demo-list.9611" (presumably the
messages posted to the list in November 1996), you would put the lines

	get demo-list profile.form
	get demo-list demo-list.9611

in your mail to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.

VII.	GETTING MORE HELP

To contact a human site manager, send mail to Majordomo-Owner@palawatr.co.th
.
To contact the owner of a specific list, send mail to that list's
approval address, which is formed by adding "-approval" to the user-name
portion of the list's address.  For instance, to contact the list owner
for demo-list@palawatr.co.th
, you would send mail to demo-list-approval@palawatr.co.th
.

To get another copy of this help message, send mail to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th

with a line saying

	help

in the message body.

VIII.	COMMAND SUMMARY FOR ADVANCED USERS

In the description below items contained in []'s are optional. When
providing the item, do not include the []'s around it.  Items in angle
brackets, such as <address>, are meta-symbols that should be replaced
by appropriate text without the angle brackets.

It understands the following commands:

    subscribe <list> [<address>]
	Subscribe yourself (or <address> if specified) to the named <list>.
	
    unsubscribe <list> [<address>]
	Unsubscribe yourself (or <address> if specified) from the named <list>.
	"unsubscribe *" will remove you (or <address>) from all lists.  This
	_may not_ work if you have subscribed using multiple addresses.

    get <list> <filename>
        Get a file related to <list>.

    index <list>
        Return an index of files you can "get" for <list>.

    which [<address>]
	Find out which lists you (or <address> if specified) are on.

    who <list>
	Find out who is on the named <list>.

    info <list>
	Retrieve the general introductory information for the named <list>.

    intro <list>
	Retrieve the introductory message sent to new users.  Non-subscribers
	may not be able to retrieve this.

    lists
	Show the lists served by this Majordomo server.

    help
	Retrieve this message.

    end
	Stop processing commands (useful if your mailer adds a signature).

Commands should be sent in the body of an email message to
"Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
". Multiple commands can be processed provided
each occurs on a separate line.

Commands in the "Subject:" line are NOT processed.

If you have any questions or problems, please contact
"Majordomo-Owner@palawatr.co.th
".


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jun 18 10:42:47 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (xitami@lists.xitami.org)
