**** Help for Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:


This help message is being sent to you from the Majordomo mailing list
management system at Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.

This is version 1.94.5 of Majordomo.

If you're familiar with mail servers, an advanced user's summary of
Majordomo's commands appears at the end of this message.

Majordomo is an automated system which allows users to subscribe
and unsubscribe to mailing lists, and to retrieve files from list
archives.

You can interact with the Majordomo software by sending it commands
in the body of mail messages addressed to "Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
".
Please do not put your commands on the subject line; Majordomo does
not process commands in the subject line.

You may put multiple Majordomo commands in the same mail message.
Put each command on a line by itself.

If you use a "signature block" at the end of your mail, Majordomo may
mistakenly believe each line of your message is a command; you will
then receive spurious error messages.  To keep this from happening,
either put a line starting with a hyphen ("-") before your signature,
or put a line with just the word

	end

on it in the same place.  This will stop the Majordomo software from
processing your signature as bad commands.

Here are some of the things you can do using Majordomo:

I.	FINDING OUT WHICH LISTS ARE ON THIS SYSTEM

To get a list of publicly-available mailing lists on this system, put the
following line in the body of your mail message to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	lists

Each line will contain the name of a mailing list and a brief description
of the list.

To get more information about a particular list, use the "info" command,
supplying the name of the list.  For example, if the name of the list 
about which you wish information is "demo-list", you would put the line

	info demo-list

in the body of the mail message.

II.	SUBSCRIBING TO A LIST

Once you've determined that you wish to subscribe to one or more lists on
this system, you can send commands to Majordomo to have it add you to the
list, so you can begin receiving mailings.

To receive list mail at the address from which you're sending your mail,
simply say "subscribe" followed by the list's name:

	subscribe demo-list

If for some reason you wish to have the mailings go to a different address
(a friend's address, a specific other system on which you have an account,
or an address which is more correct than the one that automatically appears 
in the "From:" header on the mail you send), you would add that address to
the command.  For instance, if you're sending a request from your work
account, but wish to receive "demo-list" mail at your personal account
(for which we will use "jqpublic@my-isp.com" as an example), you'd put
the line

	subscribe demo-list jqpublic@my-isp.com

in the mail message body.

Based on configuration decisions made by the list owners, you may be added 
to the mailing list automatically.  You may also receive notification
that an authorization key is required for subscription.  Another message
will be sent to the address to be subscribed (which may or may not be the
same as yours) containing the key, and directing the user to send a
command found in that message back to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.  (This can be
a bit of extra hassle, but it helps keep you from being swamped in extra
email by someone who forged requests from your address.)  You may also
get a message that your subscription is being forwarded to the list owner
for approval; some lists have waiting lists, or policies about who may
subscribe.  If your request is forwarded for approval, the list owner
should contact you soon after your request.

Upon subscribing, you should receive an introductory message, containing
list policies and features.  Save this message for future reference; it
will also contain exact directions for unsubscribing.  If you lose the
intro mail and would like another copy of the policies, send this message
to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	intro demo-list

(substituting, of course, the real name of your list for "demo-list").

III.	UNSUBSCRIBING FROM MAILING LISTS

Your original intro message contains the exact command which should be
used to remove your address from the list.  However, in most cases, you
may simply send the command "unsubscribe" followed by the list name:

	unsubscribe demo-list

(This command may fail if your provider has changed the way your
address is shown in your mail.)

To remove an address other than the one from which you're sending
the request, give that address in the command:

	unsubscribe demo-list jqpublic@my-isp.com

In either of these cases, you can tell Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
 to remove
the address in question from all lists on this server by using "*"
in place of the list name:

	unsubscribe *
	unsubscribe * jqpublic@my-isp.com

IV.	FINDING THE LISTS TO WHICH AN ADDRESS IS SUBSCRIBED

To find the lists to which your address is subscribed, send this command
in the body of a mail message to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	which

You can look for other addresses, or parts of an address, by specifying
the text for which Majordomo should search.  For instance, to find which
users at my-isp.com are subscribed to which lists, you might send the
command

	which my-isp.com

Note that many list owners completely or fully disable the "which"
command, considering it a privacy violation.

V.	FINDING OUT WHO'S SUBSCRIBED TO A LIST

To get a list of the addresses on a particular list, you may use the
"who" command, followed by the name of the list:

	who demo-list

Note that many list owners allow only a list's subscribers to use the
"who" command, or disable it completely, believing it to be a privacy
violation.

VI.	RETRIEVING FILES FROM A LIST'S ARCHIVES

Many list owners keep archives of files associated with a list.  These
may include:
- back issues of the list
- help files, user profiles, and other documents associated with the list
- daily, monthly, or yearly archives for the list

To find out if a list has any files associated with it, use the "index"
command:

	index demo-list

If you see files in which you're interested, you may retrieve them by
using the "get" command and specifying the list name and archive filename.
For instance, to retrieve the files called "profile.form" (presumably a
form to fill out with your profile) and "demo-list.9611" (presumably the
messages posted to the list in November 1996), you would put the lines

	get demo-list profile.form
	get demo-list demo-list.9611

in your mail to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.

VII.	GETTING MORE HELP

To contact a human site manager, send mail to Majordomo-Owner@palawatr.co.th
.
To contact the owner of a specific list, send mail to that list's
approval address, which is formed by adding "-approval" to the user-name
portion of the list's address.  For instance, to contact the list owner
for demo-list@palawatr.co.th
, you would send mail to demo-list-approval@palawatr.co.th
.

To get another copy of this help message, send mail to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th

with a line saying

	help

in the message body.

VIII.	COMMAND SUMMARY FOR ADVANCED USERS

In the description below items contained in []'s are optional. When
providing the item, do not include the []'s around it.  Items in angle
brackets, such as <address>, are meta-symbols that should be replaced
by appropriate text without the angle brackets.

It understands the following commands:

    subscribe <list> [<address>]
	Subscribe yourself (or <address> if specified) to the named <list>.
	
    unsubscribe <list> [<address>]
	Unsubscribe yourself (or <address> if specified) from the named <list>.
	"unsubscribe *" will remove you (or <address>) from all lists.  This
	_may not_ work if you have subscribed using multiple addresses.

    get <list> <filename>
        Get a file related to <list>.

    index <list>
        Return an index of files you can "get" for <list>.

    which [<address>]
	Find out which lists you (or <address> if specified) are on.

    who <list>
	Find out who is on the named <list>.

    info <list>
	Retrieve the general introductory information for the named <list>.

    intro <list>
	Retrieve the introductory message sent to new users.  Non-subscribers
	may not be able to retrieve this.

    lists
	Show the lists served by this Majordomo server.

    help
	Retrieve this message.

    end
	Stop processing commands (useful if your mailer adds a signature).

Commands should be sent in the body of an email message to
"Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
". Multiple commands can be processed provided
each occurs on a separate line.

Commands in the "Subject:" line are NOT processed.

If you have any questions or problems, please contact
"Majordomo-Owner@palawatr.co.th
".

**** Help for Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:


This help message is being sent to you from the Majordomo mailing list
management system at Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.

This is version 1.94.5 of Majordomo.

If you're familiar with mail servers, an advanced user's summary of
Majordomo's commands appears at the end of this message.

Majordomo is an automated system which allows users to subscribe
and unsubscribe to mailing lists, and to retrieve files from list
archives.

You can interact with the Majordomo software by sending it commands
in the body of mail messages addressed to "Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
".
Please do not put your commands on the subject line; Majordomo does
not process commands in the subject line.

You may put multiple Majordomo commands in the same mail message.
Put each command on a line by itself.

If you use a "signature block" at the end of your mail, Majordomo may
mistakenly believe each line of your message is a command; you will
then receive spurious error messages.  To keep this from happening,
either put a line starting with a hyphen ("-") before your signature,
or put a line with just the word

	end

on it in the same place.  This will stop the Majordomo software from
processing your signature as bad commands.

Here are some of the things you can do using Majordomo:

I.	FINDING OUT WHICH LISTS ARE ON THIS SYSTEM

To get a list of publicly-available mailing lists on this system, put the
following line in the body of your mail message to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	lists

Each line will contain the name of a mailing list and a brief description
of the list.

To get more information about a particular list, use the "info" command,
supplying the name of the list.  For example, if the name of the list 
about which you wish information is "demo-list", you would put the line

	info demo-list

in the body of the mail message.

II.	SUBSCRIBING TO A LIST

Once you've determined that you wish to subscribe to one or more lists on
this system, you can send commands to Majordomo to have it add you to the
list, so you can begin receiving mailings.

To receive list mail at the address from which you're sending your mail,
simply say "subscribe" followed by the list's name:

	subscribe demo-list

If for some reason you wish to have the mailings go to a different address
(a friend's address, a specific other system on which you have an account,
or an address which is more correct than the one that automatically appears 
in the "From:" header on the mail you send), you would add that address to
the command.  For instance, if you're sending a request from your work
account, but wish to receive "demo-list" mail at your personal account
(for which we will use "jqpublic@my-isp.com" as an example), you'd put
the line

	subscribe demo-list jqpublic@my-isp.com

in the mail message body.

Based on configuration decisions made by the list owners, you may be added 
to the mailing list automatically.  You may also receive notification
that an authorization key is required for subscription.  Another message
will be sent to the address to be subscribed (which may or may not be the
same as yours) containing the key, and directing the user to send a
command found in that message back to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.  (This can be
a bit of extra hassle, but it helps keep you from being swamped in extra
email by someone who forged requests from your address.)  You may also
get a message that your subscription is being forwarded to the list owner
for approval; some lists have waiting lists, or policies about who may
subscribe.  If your request is forwarded for approval, the list owner
should contact you soon after your request.

Upon subscribing, you should receive an introductory message, containing
list policies and features.  Save this message for future reference; it
will also contain exact directions for unsubscribing.  If you lose the
intro mail and would like another copy of the policies, send this message
to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	intro demo-list

(substituting, of course, the real name of your list for "demo-list").

III.	UNSUBSCRIBING FROM MAILING LISTS

Your original intro message contains the exact command which should be
used to remove your address from the list.  However, in most cases, you
may simply send the command "unsubscribe" followed by the list name:

	unsubscribe demo-list

(This command may fail if your provider has changed the way your
address is shown in your mail.)

To remove an address other than the one from which you're sending
the request, give that address in the command:

	unsubscribe demo-list jqpublic@my-isp.com

In either of these cases, you can tell Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
 to remove
the address in question from all lists on this server by using "*"
in place of the list name:

	unsubscribe *
	unsubscribe * jqpublic@my-isp.com

IV.	FINDING THE LISTS TO WHICH AN ADDRESS IS SUBSCRIBED

To find the lists to which your address is subscribed, send this command
in the body of a mail message to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
:

	which

You can look for other addresses, or parts of an address, by specifying
the text for which Majordomo should search.  For instance, to find which
users at my-isp.com are subscribed to which lists, you might send the
command

	which my-isp.com

Note that many list owners completely or fully disable the "which"
command, considering it a privacy violation.

V.	FINDING OUT WHO'S SUBSCRIBED TO A LIST

To get a list of the addresses on a particular list, you may use the
"who" command, followed by the name of the list:

	who demo-list

Note that many list owners allow only a list's subscribers to use the
"who" command, or disable it completely, believing it to be a privacy
violation.

VI.	RETRIEVING FILES FROM A LIST'S ARCHIVES

Many list owners keep archives of files associated with a list.  These
may include:
- back issues of the list
- help files, user profiles, and other documents associated with the list
- daily, monthly, or yearly archives for the list

To find out if a list has any files associated with it, use the "index"
command:

	index demo-list

If you see files in which you're interested, you may retrieve them by
using the "get" command and specifying the list name and archive filename.
For instance, to retrieve the files called "profile.form" (presumably a
form to fill out with your profile) and "demo-list.9611" (presumably the
messages posted to the list in November 1996), you would put the lines

	get demo-list profile.form
	get demo-list demo-list.9611

in your mail to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
.

VII.	GETTING MORE HELP

To contact a human site manager, send mail to Majordomo-Owner@palawatr.co.th
.
To contact the owner of a specific list, send mail to that list's
approval address, which is formed by adding "-approval" to the user-name
portion of the list's address.  For instance, to contact the list owner
for demo-list@palawatr.co.th
, you would send mail to demo-list-approval@palawatr.co.th
.

To get another copy of this help message, send mail to Majordomo@palawatr.co.th

with a line saying

	help

in the message body.

VIII.	COMMAND SUMMARY FOR ADVANCED USERS

In the description below items contained in []'s are optional. When
providing the item, do not include the []'s around it.  Items in angle
brackets, such as <address>, are meta-symbols that should be replaced
by appropriate text without the angle brackets.

It understands the following commands:

    subscribe <list> [<address>]
	Subscribe yourself (or <address> if specified) to the named <list>.
	
    unsubscribe <list> [<address>]
	Unsubscribe yourself (or <address> if specified) from the named <list>.
	"unsubscribe *" will remove you (or <address>) from all lists.  This
	_may not_ work if you have subscribed using multiple addresses.

    get <list> <filename>
        Get a file related to <list>.

    index <list>
        Return an index of files you can "get" for <list>.

    which [<address>]
	Find out which lists you (or <address> if specified) are on.

    who <list>
	Find out who is on the named <list>.

    info <list>
	Retrieve the general introductory information for the named <list>.

    intro <list>
	Retrieve the introductory message sent to new users.  Non-subscribers
	may not be able to retrieve this.

    lists
	Show the lists served by this Majordomo server.

    help
	Retrieve this message.

    end
	Stop processing commands (useful if your mailer adds a signature).

Commands should be sent in the body of an email message to
"Majordomo@palawatr.co.th
". Multiple commands can be processed provided
each occurs on a separate line.

Commands in the "Subject:" line are NOT processed.

If you have any questions or problems, please contact
"Majordomo-Owner@palawatr.co.th
".


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jun 18 11:46:50 2001

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 19 01:54:39 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bernd Luevelsmeyer)
Date: Tue, 19 Jun 2001 02:54:39 +0200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami on FreeBSD
Message-ID: <20010619005439.D832DB8103@christel.heitec.net>

Hi,

I'd like to introduce myself as the maintainer of the Xitami port on
FreeBSD.

Being the maintainer means, I'll have to see to it that Xitami compiles,
installs and runs well on the FreeBSD platform. Apart from patching some
sources and providing a proper makefile, this basically boils down to
watching the xitami web site for announcements, and the rest is waiting
for problem-mails from users.

Hence, if you have any problems with or questions concerning Xitami on
FreeBSD, I'd appreciate a mail about it.

I can state that for me, Xitami runs just fine, at least the HTTP and
CGI part of it (I don't use the FTP part because FreeBSD has a FTP
server of its own). I'd like the log to be written via the syslog daemon
though, rather than directly into files.

In case you wonder what FreeBSD is, it's an open-source Unix, closely
related to NetBSD and OpenBSD; please see http://www.freebsd.org/ for
details. You find the Xitami port listet on
http://www.freebsd.org/ports/www.html .

Thanks,
	Bernd

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 19 01:55:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Don Gordon)
Date: Tue, 19 Jun 2001 08:55:57 +0800
Subject: [Xitami] Password problems
References: <200106180931.VAA03108@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>
Message-ID: <000c01c0f85a$99d9b260$830a5f82@hm.uwa.edu.au>

Using Xitami v2.4d9 on Windows 98. Have set up directory password list in
defaults.aut. This setup works fine except with IE when it encounters a web
page that contains 2 Real Audio files. The page loads ok but when you click
on the play button IE requests the Username & Password again before it will
play the file. The problem does not occur if password restrictions are
removed.

I have waisted many an hour trying various configurations and HTML code but
have had no success. Any help would be great before I try some alternative
password protection software.

Thanks Don



From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 19 11:01:50 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 19 Jun 2001 22:01:50 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Password problems
In-Reply-To: Message from "Don Gordon" <dgordon@cyllene.uwa.edu.au>
 of "Tue, 19 Jun 2001 08:55:57 +0800." <000c01c0f85a$99d9b260$830a5f82@hm.uwa.edu.au>
Message-ID: <200106191001.WAA19757@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <000c01c0f85a$99d9b260$830a5f82@hm.uwa.edu.au>, "Don Gordon" writes:
>Using Xitami v2.4d9 on Windows 98. Have set up directory password list in
>defaults.aut. This setup works fine except with IE when it encounters a web
>page that contains 2 Real Audio files. The page loads ok but when you click
>on the play button IE requests the Username & Password again before it will
>play the file. The problem does not occur if password restrictions are
>removed.

Is it IE requesting the username/password again?  Or real player?

There's two things I can think of which might be going on here: 
(a) the files are in different directories, and you've got two sets of
    protections being applied, with different realms.  You can work 
    around this problem by setting the realm name in the .aut file
    for both protected directories to be the same (and making sure the
    same usernames/passwords apply to both).

(b) IE (which gets the authentication for the HTML page) and real player
    (which gets the authentication for the audio) do not talk to each
    other to exchange authentication information.  Which mean that both
    have to ask for that information.  This is certainly the case when
    real player is used externally, but I'm not sure if it is the case
    when it is embedded in a webpage.

Basically if you are going to password protect both HTML and audio, and
use two applications which don't talk to each other to exchange password
information, then both will have to ask the user for the password
information.

There are ways to design a system that protects the HTML and audio
without requiring the password to be entered twice, but it requires
server-side code (CGIs, LRWP, servlets, etc), and doing much of the
server-side authentication handling yourself, rather than relying on the
webservers build in basic authentication.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 19 11:08:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 19 Jun 2001 22:08:59 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami on FreeBSD
In-Reply-To: Message from Bernd Luevelsmeyer <bdluevel@heitec.net>
 of "Tue, 19 Jun 2001 02:54:39 +0200." <20010619005439.D832DB8103@christel.heitec.net>
Message-ID: <200106191008.WAA19920@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <20010619005439.D832DB8103@christel.heitec.net>, Bernd Luevelsmeyer w
rites:
>I'd like to introduce myself as the maintainer of the Xitami port on FreeBSD.

Hi.  I'd wondered who it was that was maintaining the FreeBSD port.

>I can state that for me, Xitami runs just fine, at least the HTTP and
>CGI part of it (I don't use the FTP part because FreeBSD has a FTP
>server of its own). I'd like the log to be written via the syslog daemon
>though, rather than directly into files.

It's good to hear it works well.  FWIW, most webservers write their
own logfiles (eg, Apache does as well, as well as almost all the "tiny"
http servesr I've seen), because they have special requirements for log
files which syslog doesn't handle quite so well.

We're in the process of trying to revamp the build system for all our
open source software tools to make it a little more flexible, and
hopefully a little more unix friendly.  (I develop mainly under Debian
Linux, but a number of the other iMatix developers are more Windows
focused, and this shows in a few places in Xitami.)

If there are particular things that cause a problem with the FreeBSD
port which we could look at please let me know, either directly or
ideally on the Xitami-Dev mailing list (you can subscribe at:

http://lists.xitami.org./mailman/listinfo/xitami-dev

or by emailing xitami-dev-request@lists.xitami.org)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun 20 07:37:29 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Don Gordon)
Date: Wed, 20 Jun 2001 14:37:29 +0800
Subject: [Xitami] Password problems
References: <200106191001.WAA19757@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>
Message-ID: <000701c0f953$7b0faac0$830a5f82@hm.uwa.edu.au>

Thank you for the reply.

The HTML file is located in a password protected directory while the sound
file (109k) and movie file (188k) are in subdirectories of the above. The
problem does not occur in Netscape and is occasionally fixed if the page is
refreshed in IE, but not always. I have also experimented using .ra as well
as .rpm files, no difference. The problem does not occur if the web page has
only one RealAudio file or if tested on the same computer as the server. I
have also tried setting same usernames and passwords to the subdirectories
with no effect.

You can check the test site at http://130.95.10.131/test/lesson01-08.html.
The username and password are both "test". The site is normally set up for
an intranet so loading may be slow. If by some small chance the page plays
normally, clear IE's temporary files and reload.

Further assistance would be appreciated.

----- Original Message -----
From: "Ewen McNeill" <ewen@imatix.com>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Tuesday, June 19, 2001 6:01 PM
Subject: Re: [Xitami] Password problems


> In message <000c01c0f85a$99d9b260$830a5f82@hm.uwa.edu.au>, "Don Gordon"
writes:
> >Using Xitami v2.4d9 on Windows 98. Have set up directory password list in
> >defaults.aut. This setup works fine except with IE when it encounters a
web
> >page that contains 2 Real Audio files. The page loads ok but when you
click
> >on the play button IE requests the Username & Password again before it
will
> >play the file. The problem does not occur if password restrictions are
> >removed.
>
> Is it IE requesting the username/password again?  Or real player?
>
> There's two things I can think of which might be going on here:
> (a) the files are in different directories, and you've got two sets of
>     protections being applied, with different realms.  You can work
>     around this problem by setting the realm name in the .aut file
>     for both protected directories to be the same (and making sure the
>     same usernames/passwords apply to both).
>
> (b) IE (which gets the authentication for the HTML page) and real player
>     (which gets the authentication for the audio) do not talk to each
>     other to exchange authentication information.  Which mean that both
>     have to ask for that information.  This is certainly the case when
>     real player is used externally, but I'm not sure if it is the case
>     when it is embedded in a webpage.
>
> Basically if you are going to password protect both HTML and audio, and
> use two applications which don't talk to each other to exchange password
> information, then both will have to ask the user for the password
> information.
>
> There are ways to design a system that protects the HTML and audio
> without requiring the password to be entered twice, but it requires
> server-side code (CGIs, LRWP, servlets, etc), and doing much of the
> server-side authentication handling yourself, rather than relying on the
> webservers build in basic authentication.
>
> Ewen
>
> --
> Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com
>
> --
> Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
> To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami
>


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun 20 09:25:11 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 20 Jun 2001 20:25:11 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Password problems
In-Reply-To: Message from "Don Gordon" <dgordon@cyllene.uwa.edu.au>
 of "Wed, 20 Jun 2001 14:37:29 +0800." <000701c0f953$7b0faac0$830a5f82@hm.uwa.edu.au>
Message-ID: <200106200825.UAA31398@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <000701c0f953$7b0faac0$830a5f82@hm.uwa.edu.au>, "Don Gordon" writes:
>The HTML file is located in a password protected directory while the sound
>file (109k) and movie file (188k) are in subdirectories of the above. The
>problem does not occur in Netscape and is occasionally fixed if the page is
>refreshed in IE, but not always. I have also experimented using .ra as well
>as .rpm files, no difference. 

Changing file type probably won't help; and if you change to the real
"this is where to get the audio/video" index files (.rpu? I forget),
then the problem wil probably get worse.

>The problem does not occur if the web page has only one RealAudio file or 
>if tested on the same computer as the server. I have also tried setting 
>same usernames and passwords to the subdirectories with no effect.

The default for subdirectories is to use the settings of the parent that
is protected, and this seems to be what is happening in your case.
However I'm puzzled by your statement that it doesn't happen if there is
only one RealAudio file on the page; the factors I gave before would
leave it either working or not working with 1 or more files on the page.

What you might want to try doing is turning on the Xitami server
debugging ([Server] debug=1), and then try loading the page.  Once
you've done that look at debug/debug.log to see what queries Xitami
received, and how it handled them.  My guess is that for some reason one
of the queries must be missing the username/password -- but I'm puzzled
why including two real files on the page causes that when including just
one doesn't.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Subject: [Xitami] Cgi problems
In-Reply-To: Message from "Kevin" <kev@socal.rr.com>
 of "Wed, 13 Jun 2001 16:48:27 MST." <000201c0f463$5dfd60c0$0600a8c0@socal.rr.com>
Message-ID: <200106201227.AAA01659@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <000201c0f463$5dfd60c0$0600a8c0@socal.rr.com>, "Kevin" writes:
>Using 2.4D9 Xitami server,activestate perl,windows ME,cgi enabled.
>I am able to execute an image-based counter cgi successfully if I link
>directly to the cgi.  Ie. http://host.com/cgi-bin/mycgi.pl
>But when using SSI call to the cgi inside a .html page the cgi is not
>exectuted and no cgierr is generated.

By default (and we recommend) .html files are not processed for ssi tags
(it is too much of an overhead).

>If I change the extension of the same page to .shtml then the page is
>not shown and I get a 500 internal server error.  Once again not cgierr
>is generated.

There is some problem in calling perl.  Make sure you have Perl
installed in a directory like c:\perl (ie, preferably with no spaces in
its path name), and your PATH includes c:\perl\bin in it.  If that
doesn't help, you'll need to tell us more about the "500 internal server
error" that you get -- the message includes details about what went
wrong which can be helpful in figuring out the problem.   Until perl can
be started, you probably won't see anything in cgierr.log.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun 20 13:41:14 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 21 Jun 2001 00:41:14 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] filters, pdf, c
In-Reply-To: Message from Shane D Pinder <shane.pinder@usask.ca>
 of "Thu, 19 Apr 2001 11:22:59 EST." <3ADF0299.C7BD06CA@usask.ca>
Message-ID: <200106201241.AAA01905@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <3ADF0299.C7BD06CA@usask.ca>, Shane D Pinder writes:
>Ordinarily, if a client downloads a large .pdf file, the user can see a 
>progress indication that reassures them that the file is being transferred.
>[With filter, do not]

The progress indication can only be displayed if the total length to be
sent is known; for some reason it seems that this information is being
lost/omitted with the method you are using (or being ignored).  The
Content-Length: header usually contains this information, and Xitami
should preserve this where possible.

>          printf("Content-length: %u\nContent-Type: application/pdf\n\n",
>                 fsize);

Random thought: does it make any difference if you use Content-Length:
for the header name, rather than Content-length:?  IIRC it's not
supposed to be case sensitive, but perhaps something is treating it as
case sensitive?

If you are able to do so, you might also want to capture the headers
sent back to the browser (eg, network traffic snooping) and see if the
Content-Length: header is still present, and has the right value in it.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun 20 16:51:59 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Patrick Olson)
Date: Wed, 20 Jun 2001 09:51:59 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] Lack of SSI, shtml support
References: <007c01c0f96c$3e20e020$01000084@triggerhippie> <002001c0f971$1e0c5800$123d60cb@cable.net.nz> <002a01c0f993$498a8f20$01000084@triggerhippie>
Message-ID: <3B30C69E.74449970@qwest.net>

This is how I got Perl running in Xitami
it allows me to use,

<!--#exec cgi="/cgi-bin/test.pl" -->

This SSI command
which is a potential security risk for your system
is only accepted if the environment variable
SSI_INSECURE is set to 'yes'
Under Windows NT
in the System Control Panel
under 'Environment
-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
Start->Settings->Control Panel

Double click on System

>From the pop-up box select the Environment tab

 In the Variable entry field type SSI_INSECURE
 In the Value entry field type YES
 (Make sure it goes where you want it,
  System Variables probably.)

Click OK

Reboot?  (I don't know if this is required.)
-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

under Windows 95/98 by adding
SET SSI_INSECURE=yes to the autoexec.bat.
to run SSI.
If Perl is installed correctly?
On a windows system,
You then should be able to call
Perl from anywhere in your system.
This allows the shebang to be #! perl -w
and does not need to be like this
#! c:\perl\bin\perl.exe
this also allows the use of
#! /usr/bin/perl
for the shebang. so as long
as we don't use win32 specific modules
or system calls we can keep our programs
cross platform Compatible.

Running Windows98
Xitami v2.4d6

in your
autoexec.bat

SET PATH=C:\PERL\BIN;%PATH%
SET SSI_INSECURE=YES

defaults.cfg
[Filter]
    .shtm=perlssi
    .shtml=perlssi
    .ssi=perlssi
[Ssi]
    Enabled=1
    Exec=1

hope this helps
http://www.isonline.com/xitami/2000/Jun/Msgs/l2w81135.html
http://127.0.0.1/xitami/index5.htm
http://127.0.0.1/xitami/index6.htm

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Jun 20 22:02:51 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Roberto R. Morelli)
Date: Wed, 20 Jun 2001 14:02:51 -0700
Subject: [Xitami] Lack of SSI, shtml support
References: <007c01c0f96c$3e20e020$01000084@triggerhippie> <002001c0f971$1e0c5800$123d60cb@cable.net.nz> <002a01c0f993$498a8f20$01000084@triggerhippie> <3B30C69E.74449970@qwest.net>

Folks,

There is another way, I think better. I have a site
http://www.altair7.com/index.html that uses a perl script for opening page,
see for your self.

I do not have the SSI_INSECURE set.  I do have MIME types defined as following
for the master config:

	 .pl = c:\perl\bin\perlis.dll
	.cgi = c:\perl\bin\perlis.dll

This solved all my problems.

Steps:

1. http://127.0.0.1/admin
2. configuration -> mime
3. enter the above values
4. save
5. click on restart from the main page

Done.

With that done, then this works:

	http://www.altair7.com/cgi-bin/od.pl

This works with xitami 2.4d1 through 7 and xitami pro versions.

Hope that helps, always make sure that you protect your perl scripts.

Cheers,
-Roberto

"Roberto R. Morelli" wrote:
> 
> Folks,
> 
> There is another way, I think better. I have a site
> http://www.altair7.com/index.html that uses a perl script for opening page,
> see for your self.
> 
> I do not have the SSI_INSECURE set.  I do have MIME types defined as following
> for the master config:
> 
>          .pl = c:\perl\bin\perlis.dll
>         .cgi = c:\perl\bin\perlis.dll
> 
> This solved all my problems.
> 
> Steps:
> 
> 1. http://127.0.0.1/admin
> 2. configuration -> mime
> 3. enter the above values
> 4. save
> 5. click on restart from the main page
> 
> Done.
> 
> With that done, then this works:
> 
>         http://www.altair7.com/cgi-bin/od.pl
> 
> This works with xitami 2.4d1 through 7 and xitami pro versions.
> 
> Hope that helps, always make sure that you protect your perl scripts.
> 
> Cheers,
> -Roberto

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Michael S. Kazarin)

Subject: [Xitami] Lack of SSI, shtml support (environment var)
References: <007c01c0f96c$3e20e020$01000084@triggerhippie> <002001c0f971$1e0c5800$123d60cb@cable.net.nz> <002a01c0f993$498a8f20$01000084@triggerhippie> <3B30C69E.74449970@qwest.net>
Message-ID: <00be01c0fa4c$aa1d4f80$659305c3@futeltra>



| This is how I got Perl running in Xitami
| it allows me to use,
|
| <!--#exec cgi="/cgi-bin/test.pl" -->
|
| This SSI command
| which is a potential security risk for your system
| is only accepted if the environment variable
| SSI_INSECURE is set to 'yes'
| Under Windows NT
| in the System Control Panel
| under 'Environment

This is not true for me on W2Ksp2 Xitami2.5b5.  <!--#exec
cgi="/cgi-bin/test.pl" --> will run pretty well without ssi_insecure=yes.
The latter only needed to run   #exec cmd   constructs, which certainly can
expose you to risk much more than your own scripts. Therefore, I would NOT
recommend to set SSI_INSECURE=YES

Mike

>Access.log (Nescape) - both RA files play.

>130.95.10.132 - test [21/Jun/2001:08:58:49 +0800] "GET /test/Sounds/L01-08.rpm HTTP/1.0" 304 0
>130.95.10.132 - test [21/Jun/2001:08:58:49 +0800] "GET /test/Movies/L01s08-1.rpm HTTP/1.0" 304 0

>Access.log (IE) - soud played ok, movie didn't (200 code, not 304).

>130.95.10.132 - test [21/Jun/2001:08:56:07 +0800] "GET /test/Sounds/L01-08.ra HTTP/1.1" 304 0
>130.95.10.132 - test [21/Jun/2001:08:56:07 +0800] "GET /test/Sounds/L01-08.ra HTTP/1.1" 304 0
>130.95.10.132 - test [21/Jun/2001:08:56:07 +0800] "GET /test/Movies/L01s08-1.ra HTTP/1.1" 200 191945
>130.95.10.132 - test [21/Jun/2001:08:56:07 +0800] "GET /test/Movies/L01s08-1.ra HTTP/1.1" 200 191945

This is just strange.  304 is "not modified" which means "the copy
you've already got is up to date, you can use that"; 200 is "found" and
means "here you go, here's a copy of the thing you requested".

In _both_ cases it should play just fine, as both bits of audio are
available without apparent problems.

What I'm really puzzled about is IE getting a 304 return on both files
(ie, being told the local copies are fine), and then deciding it needs
to get a copy of them _anyway_.  It almost looks like IE doesn't believe
the webserver when it says the existing files are okay!

I see you're using IE 5.0: is this the 5.0 with the security problems,
or the 5.01 fixed version (I don't know if they report different
User-Agent headings).  In either case I would expect it to work, but
apparently it isn't working "as expected".

>I have had a look at Paul Reid's site which works fine with multiple RA 
>files and password. The difference is that my RA files are embedded 
>which seems to cause the problem in IE. This problem is starting to look 
>like a too hard basket case. Any further advice would be gratefully 
>accepted.

One thing you might want to consider if it's causing you a lot of pain
is "security through obscurity" -- put the RA files in a non-password
protected directory, and just only link to them from your hidden page.
Obviously anyone who knew the URL would then be able to get the RA
files, but hopefully IE will then manage to cope.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

> One thing you might want to consider if it's causing you a lot of pain
is "security through obscurity" -- put the RA files in a non-password
protected directory, and just only link to them from your hidden page.

I posted to Don off-list; I didn't want to tell everybody the details of my
"security through obscurity" trick.

But just as you say: the HTML file and a RAM file containing the URL(s) of the
media file(s) are in an Xitami-password directory; the actual media files are
in a "public" but not browsable folder (and a different machine and server,
but that should not matter). 

The security risk is that someone might capture the RAM file; or the URL in
standalone RealPlayer, and give it to unauthorized persons. 

> The difference is that my RA files are embedded which seems to cause the problem in IE. 

Don's page with embedded player is slick, I like it; but I had little luck
with embedding more than one player per page. It is supposed to work, I've
seen it work (without passwording), but it all seems very flaky to me. I think
it is a low priority at Real.Inc. 

 -PRR

I have never really played with the passwords in xitami but i did write a
perl script that checks login and password and once it confirms these it
loads up a picture and delivers it to the user ....only the script knows
where the picture is and it is therefore impossible to link to the picture
directly.

im sure that the same thing could be applied to your real audio files to
hide them.
my script allows for the originating directory to be anywhere on the drive
and it can therefore be outside the web folders.

another possibility is that you use perl to rename  the file or dir each
time it is accessed again making any links to it useless.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun 22 16:38:40 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Fri, 22 Jun 2001 11:38:40 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Why is my XITAMI server so slow?
References: <MAEPKOFMKPDCFOHCHFAFIENHCLAA.grangeway@btinternet.com> <004601c0fabc$3ac8aec0$6401a8c0@bur.adelphia.net>
Message-ID: <3B336680.3C531832@rci.rutgers.edu>

> file transfers on my LAN are where they should be now.

I have NOT had my morning coffee yet, so don't trust these numbers until you
run them through your abacus. I've probably dropped decimal points all over
the floor. So all this may be wrong. 

> 340 Megabytes in 6 minutes on my 10 MegaBit router.  

0.94 MegaBytes/Second, 7.5 Megabits/Second is excellent for a 10-speed
connection. That shows that the LAN hardware is running a full 10-speed. I
have seen a shade higher (1.1 MegaBytes/Sec) on a new 10MBPS switch-- have not
seen that since everybody else on the floor got hooked up. 

> FTP from inside my LAN  About 340 MegaBytes in 30 minutes 

Even allowing for FTP overhead, 0.189 MegaBytes/Sec (1.5 Megabits/Sec) inside
a LAN is not great, but not shocking if the line is 10 MBPS. If both computers
and the hub are supposedly working at 100 MBPS, it sucks. 

I just FTP-ed 8.3 MegaBytes from the (Xitami, P-133, 10MBPS) server down the
hall in 11 sec. 0.75 MegaBytes/Sec, 6 Megabits/Sec. 

Are the PCs old and slow? Have you burdened the FTP server with aliases or
many-many Vhosts it must figure out? (You don't have Napster running I hope.)

Note that your cable-router does NOT have to be your internal LAN hub. I have
100 MBPS around the office on this floor, but a 10 MBPS link to a router in
the basement. When I find two 100 MBPS PCs to talk to each other locally, I
get over 3 MegaBytes/Sec. (I keep a 10 MBPS card in the web server partly so
it can't clog the LAN.)

> 340 MB in 5 hours through ISP

0.019 MegaBytes per second, 150 Kilobits/Sec, sounds like a throttled
connection to me. That's 3 or 4 times better than 56K modem. That's probably
what home cable providers aim for: as you say they don't want you running a
high-traffic site on a home-price account, but I guess they don't want it to
be "worse" than a 56K phone modem. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jun 23 19:56:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dr. Martin R. Hadam)
Date: Sat, 23 Jun 2001 19:56:33 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] SMP Problem (WAS: Xitami 2.4d9/Xitami 2.5b5)
Message-ID: <E15Dre5-0001ll-00@Mail.MH-Hannover.DE>

On Mon, 11 Jun 2001 00:54:48 +1200, Ewen McNeill wrote:

 I've done some deep thinking <g> and then tested one thing I'd
apparently  forgotten (shame on me!): since the problem [see below] is
occuring on an SMP machine, I've disabled the use of both processors
using execmode and voil - Xitami is now perfectly stable again. In
case you're not familiar with execmode: this IBM utility patches an
exe/dll to only make use of one processor in an smp system. So it seems
that there is a serious new problem with threading in Xitami versions
>2.4d6 [OS/2]. This has been tested / verified on two different machines running OS/2 Warp Server SMP at FP 42/43 resp. The test version I used with execmode was the 2.5b4 patch #2 (Bernd Hohmann).

 To reiterate the problem - since its description is now some time ago:
Xitami starts and quits after a while without any further error message
(other than the one below).

 Hope that this will allow you to better trace the problem.
 
 Martin


>In message <E158S7R-0000Ee-00@Mail.MH-Hannover.DE>, "Dr. Martin R. Hadam" writes:
>> I've been moving machines and today, Xitami provided some message, for
>>the first time:
>>2001/06/08 21:32:16: smthttp: HTTP service is now running
>>Fatal error in application - aborted
>>Abort at smtsock:Check-For-Expired-Requests: (Getting-Event, Empty-Event)
>>Abnormal program termination
>
>Ah, that sort of problem.  You might want to keep an eye on whether it's
>always at the same point, or whether the problems shift around.  If they
>shift around it's most likely that something is writing to memory it
>shouldn't.  If it's always (or usually) one place, then possibly there's
>something wrong with the way that some requests are handled by smtsock.
>Unfortunately either way they're difficult to diagnose problems, since
>they're not easily reproducable.

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)

 of "Sat, 23 Jun 2001 19:56:33 +0100." <E15Dre5-0001ll-00@Mail.MH-Hannover.DE>

In message <E15Dre5-0001ll-00@Mail.MH-Hannover.DE>, "Dr. Martin R. Hadam" writes:
> I've done some deep thinking <g> and then tested one thing I'd
>apparently  forgotten (shame on me!): since the problem [see below] is
>occuring on an SMP machine, I've disabled the use of both processors
>using execmode and voil - Xitami is now perfectly stable again. 

Ah ha. 

I was going to say that Xitami didn't use threads, so I didn't see what
the problem could be, but IIRC there are a few minor uses of threads for
various auxillary things (and EMX uses threads for a few things).
(Xitami mostly works as a single process, single thread, and uses
select() and SMT to figure out what to do next.)

Our development version makes even less use of thread-related things, so
it's possible the problem might go away with that.  Unfortunately we
don't curerntly have an OS/2 development system, let alone a SMP-capable
OS/2 development system available.  However I do have a SMP Linux
development system, and I might try playing there and see if anything
breaks.

And it's useful to know that single-threaded Xitami is very stable. 

Thanks for following this up.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jun 23 20:53:35 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Dr. Martin R. Hadam)
Date: Sat, 23 Jun 2001 20:53:35 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] SMP Problem (WAS: Xitami 2.4d9/Xitami 2.5b5)
Message-ID: <E15DsXH-0001rS-00@Mail.MH-Hannover.DE>

On Sun, 24 Jun 2001 06:14:01 +1200, Ewen McNeill wrote:

>I was going to say that Xitami didn't use threads, so I didn't see what
>the problem could be, but IIRC there are a few minor uses of threads for
>various auxillary things (and EMX uses threads for a few things).
>(Xitami mostly works as a single process, single thread, and uses
>select() and SMT to figure out what to do next.)

 Well, it's listed as running on two threads here. I'm quite familiar
with the situation that I'm seeing problems that no-one else is
encountering... <g> Please note that it must have been something that
changed after v2.4d6.

>Our development version makes even less use of thread-related things, so
>it's possible the problem might go away with that.  Unfortunately we
>don't curerntly have an OS/2 development system, let alone a SMP-capable
>OS/2 development system available.  However I do have a SMP Linux
>development system, and I might try playing there and see if anything
>breaks.

 whenever you have something to test (assuming that Bernd Hohman had
volunteered to do the compilation for an OS/2 version) I'll be happy to
run it here.

>And it's useful to know that single-threaded Xitami is very stable.

 It's not making it single-threaded. Execmode only restricts the
software from accessing both processors and puts all the workload for
that package on processor #1; effectively making a given software as if
running on a uniprocessor system. From what I learned by following
other SMP-related bugs I came across it could be more of a timing
problem (or the like).

 Martin

> Does anyone know of a stable counter I can run on my server - that I can trigger from Javascript?

There are a gazillion counters that return a graphic of a number.
I'm not sure what you mean "trigger from Javascript" -- you can 
document.write almost anything. 

I have one counter, a Windows NT EXE, that I trigger from static
HTML. It returns a graphic of a number. 

I have another counter that I call from Javascript (with a
NOSCRIPT option to catch lame or hobbled browsers). It is written
in Perl and returns a static image (generally a 1x1 transparent
GIF to satisfy the browser without showing on the page) but keeps
detailed logs of hits. Another Perl script summarizes the hits,
but that isn't made public. That's for pages where I want to know
what kind of surfers are hitting, but don't want them to see how
(un)popular the site is. 

Look on the top page of Music.rutgers.edu , low on the left is
the static-call public graphic counter. I'm looking for where I
got it from... the name in it is Henn Saar, 1995.

> don't curerntly have an OS/2 development system, let alone a SMP-capable

> development system, and I might try playing there and see if anything

I've not done any multi-threaded development myself either, but AIUI, the
support for multi-threading in OS/2 is an order of magnitude more
efficient than that in ANY dialect of Unix.  If you cannot properly
"corral" multiple execution threads, perhaps Xitami needs to make a
conscious effort to disable threading.  (Given that OS/2's multi-
threading support runs to 64 processors; also given that eComStation is
going to make a cheap SMP O/S available to all those with dual Pentium
motherboards.)

> And it's useful to know that single-threaded Xitami is very stable. 

Indeed.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Jun 24 13:36:54 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
Date: Sun, 24 Jun 2001 12:36:54 GMT
Subject: [Xitami] SMP Problem (WAS: Xitami 2.4d9/Xitami 2.5b5)
Message-ID: <42702@dsl.co.uk>

In message <42685@dsl.co.uk> I wrote:
> I've not done any multi-threaded development myself either, but AIUI, the
> support for multi-threading in OS/2 is an order of magnitude more
> efficient than that in ANY dialect of Unix.  If you cannot properly
> "corral" multiple execution threads, perhaps Xitami needs to make a
> conscious effort to disable threading.  (Given that OS/2's multi-
> threading support runs to 64 processors; also given that eComStation is
> going to make a cheap SMP O/S available to all those with dual Pentium
> motherboards.)

I failed to make it clear that multi-threading in no way requires
multiple processors (as has already been mentioned elsewhere in this
thread:-)

AIUI, under Linux, creating a separate execution thread is almost as
costly as forking another process, so programs tend to do the latter
rather than the former.  In contrast under OS/2, spawning a thread is a
very cheap operation, so multi-threaded programs are more common.

References: <20010624175998.SM00258@default>
Message-ID: <3B36CD68.1242D5C3@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I then tried the DNS approach and set virtual hosting to www2.stc.com=stc.cfg but when I typed www2.stc.com in my browser's location bar, it dialed in and tried to find it on the Internet. 

You probably have a text file called "hosts". On Windows NT it
may be at C:\WINNT\system32\hosts, though it has been seen under
many names. Even Lmhosts.sam (which is really for something else,
but has been known to influence IP lookup).

It looks something like this: 

# This is a sample HOSTS file ...

#  102.54.94.97     rhino.acme.com      # source server

127.0.0.1       localhost

If typing "localhost" at your browser opens your page at
127.0.0.1, you have a hosts file somewhere (and that's why it
works). Anything on a line after "#" is ignored. 

Add some lines like 

127.0.0.1 manny

127.0.0.1 moe

127.0.0.1 jack

Save the file. 

Now, typing "manny" at your browser should open your default
127.0.0.1 page.

Now go into Xitami's Vhost settings and tell it that "manny"
points to a CFG file called "manny.cfg". In manny.cfg, point to
"O:/WebSites/mndm" as the root of the web pages for that host. Do
the same for moe and jack, except point to your other web-root
folders. 

Now typing manny, moe, or jack at your browser should open three
different web sites. 

You -may- still have trouble with your TCP stack not believing
the hosts file and going to the modem to ask a "real DNS". MS TCP
stacks can be quite dumb. 

When you get past that: I've had some trouble when web folders
are not on the same drive as Xitami. It "should" work, and often
it does, but sometimes it does not. 

Also: after setting or changing a Vhost, stop and restart Xitami.
I'm not sure if it "should" pick up the change on the fly, but my
habit is to force it to start anew.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jun 25 06:43:58 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 25 Jun 2001 01:43:58 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] How-to? Set up multiple web sites using a single static IP
 address
References: <f4.bb8ef81.2867fdee@aol.com>
Message-ID: <3B36CF9E.78492EBC@rci.rutgers.edu>

> the documentation is fairly thin on how to actually set this up. 

Open http://www.yourhost.com/admin

It wants the name and password you picked when you installed
Xitami (the name is probably "admin"). Proceed to the Admin
screen. 

Fourth button down is "VHost Wizard". Click. 

 "Virtual Host Wizard

 Create virtual host profile:  ### make up a name like "test"

 Select IP address:  ### leave blank in this case
                                                      
 Or, enter DNS host name:  ### your second domain name
                                                                                
 Web page root directory:  ### where the second set of files are
                                                                                
You can leave the rest blank. 

This Wizard really does set it all up for you: making CFG files
that point to the right place. 

Stop and re-start Xitami after the change: it is sometimes loathe
to take on a new VHost until you whack it. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Jun 25 11:03:06 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)

Subject: [Xitami] SMP Problem (WAS: Xitami 2.4d9/Xitami 2.5b5)
In-Reply-To: Message from bhk@dsl.co.uk (Brian {Hamilton Kelly})
 of "Sun, 24 Jun 2001 12:36:54 GMT." <42702@dsl.co.uk>
Message-ID: <200106251003.WAA00627@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <42702@dsl.co.uk>, Brian {Hamilton Kelly} writes:
>AIUI, under Linux, creating a separate execution thread is almost as
>costly as forking another process, so programs tend to do the latter
>rather than the former.  In contrast under OS/2, spawning a thread is a
>very cheap operation, so multi-threaded programs are more common.

Under Linux creating a new process (with fork()) is almost as cheap as
creating a new thread -- which is what you said, but the emphasis is
that creating a new process is cheap.  (Starting a new program in that
process costs more; more like starting a new process in OS/2.)

Traditionally unix does not have threads, and even those unixes that do,
do not have them in a widely portable fashion.  So processes tend to get
used instead.

However as I said, Xitami tries to buck this trend and be single
threaded, single process -- which has its advantages and disadvantages.

All that said, I'm puzzled what could be causing your problem on a SMP
machine, which is fixed by running it on a single processor, if it isn't
a threading issue.  

Can you tell me what build flags you used to build Xitami?  And which
version of the compiler and build environment?

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 26 10:52:22 2001

all ok so far, but - the cgi and perl scripts in my cgi-bin all have the #!
usr/bin/perl
path, which I wish to keep as the original host's environment, and this will
not work on Xitami. I have found the following information below under the
help/configuration documents, and wondered how I could allow these scripts
to work if at all - would I have to use aliases or something similar?

can I ultimately configure different sites to use their respective
'Shebang's' despite running on win98 se?

Please help, otherwise I may have to go back to trying to use lumbering
Apache again for the 4th time :o(

---------------------

What's the equivalent of the shebang ("#!") syntax for Win32?
Unfortunately, Win32 platforms don't provide the shebang syntax, or anything
like it.

Although Win32 systems themselves don't use the shebang, the Apache
webserver does. If you are using the Apache webserver on your Win32 system
you should put the shebang line at the top of your CGI scripts.

Your shebang line should look something like:

 #!perl

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 26 11:45:19 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 26 Jun 2001 22:45:19 +1200
Subject: [Xitami] Shebang #! question on win98
In-Reply-To: Message from "dimitri" <dimitri@easygoin.net>
 of "Tue, 26 Jun 2001 10:52:22 +0100." <001801c0fe25$c28f7340$01000084@triggerhippie>
Message-ID: <200106261045.WAA16564@pagoda.wgtn.cat-it.co.nz>

In message <001801c0fe25$c28f7340$01000084@triggerhippie>, "dimitri" writes:
>all ok so far, but - the cgi and perl scripts in my cgi-bin all have the #!
>usr/bin/perl
>path, which I wish to keep as the original host's environment,

Xitami is even more generous than Apache: providing the #! line _ends_
with "perl", _and_ the perl binary is on the Path, Xitami will run it.
(It tries the exact path first, and if that is not found, it strips off
the path name, and tries that instead.)

So put perl in c:\perl, and add c:\perl\bin to your path, then start
Xitami.  And your #!/usr/bin/perl lines should work just fine.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 26 17:41:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 26 Jun 2001 12:41:26 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Shebang #! question on win98
References: <001801c0fe25$c28f7340$01000084@triggerhippie>
Message-ID: <3B38BB36.29E496AD@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  #! usr/bin/perl path, ... will not work on Xitami.

On Xitami in DOS/Windows? Sure it does. 

The average unix interpreter and webserver wants the she-bang line to be
exact; they won't go searching for Perl.

As Ewen says, Xitami (at least when compiled for DOS/Win) is "Generous".
It knows that DOS is different, and it would be awkward to re-edit
scripts every time you move from unix to DOS. 

If the folder that the she-bang line points to doesn't exist, it pulls a
copy of PATH and starts hunting for Perl or Perl.exe. 

To prove that Xitami is pretty smart, I have some scripts with #!
/bing/bang/boom/perl , and it works. That fails, but PATH contains
d:\perl , and Xitami quickly finds it there. 

Probable problems: 

Perl Install asks if you want Perl on PATH. I hope you said Yes. Also,
you often have to shut-down and re-start Windows to get the changed
PATH. (You can force it manually, but Win98 needs a break anyway.)

Open a Command window and type PATH. If Perl's folder is on there,
re-start Xitami and it should work. If it isn't there, re-start Windows.
If you didn't let Perl Install modify PATH, open AUTOEXEC.BAT in notepad
and add it, restart.

Putting Perl in a path with a space in it (typically under "Program
Files" can give trouble. Very long (over 62 characters) paths can also
be iffy. I'm not sure if this is Xitami or Perl, but IAC nobody can
exactly duplicate MS's wacky handling of long spacy filenames. K.I.S.S.:
Keep It Short and Sweet. 

There is a limit in DOS/Win9x on the size of PATH (actually the
envoronment). If you've installed many programs that all think they
deserve to be on PATH (most don't), you may have to trim. 

In the unlikely event that you have a DOS/Win system that really does
have a /usr/bin directory, I thought that Xitami would fail if the
folder was valid and the program name wasn't right there. Mayeb I'm
wrong. If I'm right, the logical thing to do is put Perl in /usr/bin. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 26 17:51:04 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Andrew Tate)
Date: Tue, 26 Jun 2001 17:51:04 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] How-to? Set up multiple web sites using a single static IP address
In-Reply-To: <f4.bb8ef81.2867fdee@aol.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010626175104.00ad0c80@pop.surrey.ac.uk>

Hi,

Others have already replied and given some information.  The way the server decides on which site to serve up is the name given in the http request.  So for instance one of my servers is on ip 131.227.111.3 - you can try it and you get served up the  so called 'basehost.cfg' pages.  If you use www.cpe.surrey.ac.uk then it finds the string in the request and severs up the pages defined in www.cfg. 

However, this only works in recent browsers and may not be supported with light wap phones etc - I don't know.  I have just tested this and Netscape 1.0 and 1.2 give the basehost pages for www.cpe.surrey.ac.uk but version 2.0 and onwards behave properly.  I guess newer browsers pass on the request string.  Not that it matters much these days but I have no access to lightwieght browsers in personal phones and organisers. 

The suggestion to use the web admin page is good - once you have set one up then you can tweak and copy the actual file.  The main file to look at is:- 

defaults.cfg

and the lines that matter are like

[Virtual-hosts]
    Www.cpe.surrey.ac.uk=www.cfg
    Www.tates.co.uk=tates.cfg


as you see if you hit my server at 131.227.111.3 with the request string of www.cpe.surrey.ac.uk then it uses the www.cfg file for details of the web pages to serve up.  If however you use www.tates.co.uk then it looks in tates.cfg.  You can use any file name but these seemed sensible to me to keep it logical.  You can even have multiple domain names going to the same pages so you can have your own custom pages - " web site under construction "


Now file tates.cfg has 


[Accesslog]
    Cycle=5
    Cycle-arg=tates-acc%yy%mm%dd.log
    Filename=tates-access.log
    Format=CLF
    Cycle-how=0

[Alias]
    Xitami=c:/xitami/webpages/xitami

[Errorlog]
    Cycle=5
    Cycle-arg=tates-er%yy%mm%dd.log
    Filename=tates-error.log
    Format=CLFX
    Translate=1

[Rdns]
    Recurse-lookups=0

[Security]
    Filename=tates.aut
    Safepaths=0

[Server]
    Webpages=/xitami/websites/tates

[Serverlog]
    Enabled=0


so you see I mirror the normal file but put tates in place of the standard server to create log files, access files etc etc.  You also need to create tates.aut to set the authorisations.  I also use \websites as the directory under which all my virtual websites live but leave the default \webpages that Xitami sets up for basehost and other bits.

basehost.cfg is automatically picked up by xitami if there is no match hence it gets any other unknown dns name that points to the ip address or a pure ip address as in my example above. On my server I serve up a page all about the wonders of Xitami !!  The sample web pages that come with the distribution.

I have typed this quickly and hope it helps - they may be a few mistakes I am no expert.  I believe there is another way of multiple hosting where you assign multiple ip addresses to the same machine and xitami serves up the pages dependant on this but I have never done this and it does not seem to fit so well with the sort of re-direction available from isp services who will set up a redirection page for you.  It also needs an operating system able to assign multiple ips to one ethernet card or you need multiple ethernet cards...  not so easy.


Yours,

Andy Tate.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 26 19:02:24 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 26 Jun 2001 14:02:24 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] How-to? Set up multiple web sites using a single static IP
 address
References: <3.0.6.32.20010626175104.00ad0c80@pop.surrey.ac.uk>
Message-ID: <3B38CE30.8CA30D8E@rci.rutgers.edu>

> 131.227.111.3 - ... you get served ...'basehost.cfg' pages.  If you use
www.cpe.surrey.ac.uk then it finds the string in the request and serves
up the pages defined in www.cfg. 

> However, this only works in recent browsers ...I have just tested this and Netscape 1.0 and 1.2 give the basehost pages for www.cpe.surrey.ac.uk but version 2.0 and onwards behave properly.  I guess newer browsers pass on the request string.  

NetScape 2+ and IE 3+ send the URL of the page they expect to get. NS1
and IE2 don't. 

Basically, any browser made in the last 6 or 7 years will handle
name-based VHosting. 

I'm tracking browser versions on a general-interest page. I don't track
the oldest versions, but in the last 4,580 hits only 5 came from IE3, 0
from NS2, 100 from NS3. I suspect that NS1 and IE1-2 are less than NS2
and IE3, or well under 0.1%. 

Since few Win31 machines are alive, and Win95 came with IE3, the only
large clump of IE2 users will be Win NT4 machines that have avoided any
update of IE. (NT4 shipped with IE2, though many OEM installations and
all MS Office installations put something newer on.) Upgrades of NS and
IE are free. 

Those few people still using NS1 and IE2 are doing it because they want
to. They must know that the Web expects something more today; many sites
fall apart in NS1/IE2 (and yet some quite fancy sites stand up). If they
don't get the site they expect, that's really their choice.

As for palm wappers- I never saw one, in person or as a strange hit on
my site. And I know they are minimal machines. But named VHost just
means that they put the URL in the HTTP request header. They already
have the URL in their tiny mind, so it seems trivial to add it to the
request. And so many sites are really VHosted that I'd think they'd be
useless for general surfing unless they supported it. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Jun 26 22:56:22 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Tue, 26 Jun 2001 17:56:22 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Re: Running Xitami ouside of Systray in windows
References: <9EFD49E2FB59D411AABA0008C7E675C002DCDBE6@emss04m10.ems.lmco.com>
Message-ID: <3B390506.B7535AA7@rci.rutgers.edu>

I assume you are using the NT Service version.

The Service version is appropriate if you want Windows to auto-start the
service even before any user logs-on. My web server sits at the log-in
prompt for months on end, because there isn't any reason to log-on at
the terminal since Xitami starts before that as a Service.

If you or some process you wrote wants to be able to start and stop
Xitami at will, I'd think the Console version is more appropriate.

If Java can call an arbitrary DOS command, I think there is a
command-line option to kill the Service. But a stop-start mode is more
what the Console version is made for.

 -PRR

At 02:16 PM 6/27/2001 -0400, you wrote:
>     I'm sure there's a way to look at who's been accessing my XITAMI FTP
>and HTTP servers but I can't figure it out.  Where do I look.  Is this
>information in a text file?  I think I looked through all the log files but
>didn't see anything of interest.
>     Thanks and take care.

Take a look at access.log, in the logs subdirectory of wherever you installed Xitami.  You might not be able to open it while Xitami is running, since it opens and locks that file when it starts up (at least for me; WinME, Xitami 2.4d9, YMMV).
If you (or anyone else) is interested, I've written a short perl script that goes through and analyzes this file.  http://xbones.resnet.gatech.edu/cgi-bin/logview.pl if you want to try it; email me if you want the source.

-Dan Orzechowski
xbonesgt@cc.gatech.edu
http://xbones.resnet.gatech.edu

Hi Espen !

I downloaded xitami2.5b4 for beos from bebits and installed it.
The result - generally I can say that it works. I can suppose what confused
you.
This is not a gui app, it's a console version. If you accepted default
location for installation then you have to:
start the Terminal
cd /boot/apps/Xitami    (mind case sensitivity)
xitami -s (to run Xitami in background or)
xitami -S (to run in foreground, default)
Use xitami -h for options.

Anyway I encountered some problems. I belive all files included in the
package are the same as for windows distributions which I use except the
binary itself. Thus I guess it wasn't properly compiled, something wrong
with paths. For example the images located in ./webpages/images do not load
if I type http://localhost/images/image_1.gif, but they do if I type
http://localhost//images/image_1.gif. On the other hand
./webpages/xitami/images works fine and
http://localhost/xitami/images/image_1.gif displays as desired. Probably for
the same reason an image map on the front page doesn't work. When I click
for testcgi.exe url on the map, it resolves as http:/cgi-bin/testcgi.exe
CGI themselves work fine, as well as SSI.
Perhaps, some tweaking can be done with configs. Didn't have time to try it
yesterday. All I wanna say that it didn't install well from scratch as my
windows version did.

Another serious issue for me is that when Xitami is started, cpu load for my
amd duron 750 goes up to 100% and stays there until I stop the server. I
have no idea what's going wrong. Never experienced that with any other BeOS
app.

I hope this info will be of value to you and I would like to hear your
comments on whether you'll be able to get it going.

Mike.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Jun 28 17:11:06 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Thu, 28 Jun 2001 12:11:06 -0400
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami on BeOS
References: <A8C0C01156D5D311ABF20000E82D9B1F166EB0@NM01> <002701c0fedf$8f77a940$659305c3@futeltra> <006801c0ffb2$87884450$659305c3@futeltra>
Message-ID: <3B3B571A.DD1CB911@rci.rutgers.edu>

> [in BeOS] cpu load ... goes up to 100% and stays there

Does it yield? That is, when you do other work on the machine, does it
feel slow? 

I don't know BeOS, but in Windows many DOS apps will send the CPU Use
meter to the max yet the machine feels only 5%-10% slow in other
applications. 

In Windows, a proper app is supposed to give up its time slice if it has
nothing to do. DOS apps assume they own the whole machine. Many of them,
when "doing nothing" sit in a tight loop asking "Did user press a key
yet?", asking that question 750,000,000 times a second on modern CPUs.
Windows can't be sure if the DOS app's frenzy is doing something useful
or not. So if no other app is demanding cycles, the DOS app gets most of
the CPU's time. If another app does have something to do, it gets the
time it needs, and the DOS app gets just a few cycles on every loop of
the Windows task-switcher. 

Sometimes the DOS app appears to Windows to be greedy; I have a DOS
modem program that -will- slow the rest of Windows if it has trouble
opening the modem (because Windows has grabbed the modem for DUN). 

BTW, there are some tricks for time-sharing background programs in
Windows (NT). A main one is to "Stall" a DOS app when it is in the
background, so it gets no time when you are not using it. Good for a
text editor, bad for a web server. There are other priority options,
though I must note that some cause more trouble than they are worth.
(Don't put a DOS app in RealTime priority or you'll never get control
back!)

Clearly the BeOS compile of Xitami is not supporting whatever
load-sharing that BeOS has. Of course it is interesting that Xitami
works at all on a platform that isn't really a classic unix and isn't
DOS/Win or OS/2, the platforms that got specific support. 

There is of course a native web server in BeOS. And I'd guess that the
total BeOS webserver market is too small for anybody to spend a lot of
programming time on. But since Xitami itself runs on one big loop,
anybody who really knows BeOS's load-share technique (or who can find
similar code in some other BeOS application) could add a "Nothing to do
right now" flag to release the current time-slice back to BeOS.

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun 29 05:47:11 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Thu, 28 Jun 2001 23:47:11 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Screen Resolution...
In-Reply-To: <25309464.6CF8707E.0EEEC7A4@cs.com>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010628234711.007a45c0@pop.crosswinds.net>

As I was playing around with IE, I noticed that the headers contain some
extremely useful data that my CGI-based applications could use.  I have
this interesting idea that Xitami could do something horribly non-standard
and pass all of the headers onto my CGI (filter) through another
environment variable.  Here is what I propose:

1)  Create a configuration file option to turn on/off the COMPLETE_HEADERS
environment variable.
2)  During runtime, if the environment variable option is on, then the
COMPLETE_HEADERS variable is created.  Xitami stores the headers into the
environment variable as a zero-terminated URL encoded string.

Of particular interest to me (and probably a few others) are the headers:

UA-pixels: 1152x864
UA-color: color16
UA-OS: Windows NT
UA-CPU: x86

Now, I could use JavaScript to do what I want on the client end of things,
but it would be nice to just grab and parse the headers for the information
I need rather than play with cookies (we all know how much we love cookies
:)) or other similar mechanism (cookies are easier).  The only problem with
both methods is that the user might turn the headers off.  It doesn't
matter, except that the server-side method is a lot easier to code than the
cookie or JavaScript methods.

Just an idea...

                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

Try reading the official definition of HTTP v1.1 (in RFC 2068 et seq) and
you'll discover that those "headers" are completely non-standard and will
be found only on requests coming from some of the computers that have
been blessed with Mr Gates's crap.

It's just another example of Redmond "inventing" an "extension" to a
standard in order to suborn the world into using Windoze, when those
standards were designed for interoperability between ANY computer
systems.  Such extensions are best ignored.

Besides, the principle of good web page design dictate that the page
should present itself in a manner that clearly communicates its
information content to the reader, independently of any paramters such as
those above.  Remember "This page is optimized for ANY browser" is the
best precept.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Jun 29 15:33:32 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Thomas J. Hruska)
Date: Fri, 29 Jun 2001 09:33:32 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] why doesn't it work?
In-Reply-To: <20010629064341.43347.qmail@web9505.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <000d01c1004b$1570dd70$123d60cb@cable.net.nz>
Message-ID: <3.0.6.32.20010629093332.007c0420@pop.crosswinds.net>

At 11:43 PM 6/28/01 -0700, you wrote:
>I just bought a server and I networked them together

What is the "them" you are referring to?  If you bought a server, there is
only a single node on the network.  If you are attempting to interface the
server with a current lan to provide a single connection to get to the
internet, you need to set up gateway information on the machines on the lan
to point to the right place.

>with two ethernet cards in the server so the other
>computer can use the internet. I used the same IP
>address only when people try to connect they don't
>seem able to because I think it is because that it
>runs two different IP's. Do you have any idea how to help?

If you are running Xitami on the server and the server has two network
cards (what I suspect you are doing), the server's network cards need to
have their own individual IP addresses or the requests coming in will get
messed up.  To load-balance the requests, I suggest purchasing a
load-balancing switch rather than messing with a software-based solution
(really messy if you ask me).  That way, if you get another server later,
you can offload some of the load onto the newer server.

Also, the IP addresses of the network cards have to be real IP addresses on
the internet (or the firewall has to forward all connections on port 80 to
the firewall's IP to the web server).  If you want clients on the lan to
access the internet through the server (via a proxy), you have to assign
one network card with a LAN IP (10.x.x.x or 192.168.x.x number, depending
on which you use) and the other with a valid internet address.  You can't
just assign the internet address whatever you feel like using unless you
have a static IP (in which case you have to use that IP and nothing else).

Without more information on what exactly you are trying to accomplish with
the server and how Xitami fits into this, this list can't really help you
very much.


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net
Shining Light Productions -- "Meeting the needs of fellow programmers"
                  http://www.shininglightpro.com/

> my browsers don't reload the page 

Typically, browsers don't even check every time, unless you
change the defaults (which are designed for speed, not
up-to-dateness). 

In NetScape 4.5+: 

 Edit, Preferences, Advanced, Cache, 
 "Document in cache is compared to document on network..."
  - EVERY time 
 (the "once per session" and "never" options are no good for
web    authors). 

 -PRR

At 10:58 PM 6/29/01 -0500, you wrote:
>Greetings;
>
>Running V2.5b5 on NT 4.0 my browsers don't reload the page when 
>it has changed. I use IE 5.5 and Netscape 4.7. I have to force the 
>refresh or reload before I can see the changed page. (This is ctl-
>refresh in IE or shift-reload in Netscape.)
>
>I know only that this has something to do with the file date. Is Xitami 
>not sending the date to the browser? I can see that the date has 
>changed in NT explorer.

I was having problems with both browsers as well until I added some meta tags:

<meta http-equiv="expires" content="0">
<meta http-equiv="pragma" content="no-cache">

In theory this tells the browser to not cache anything and that the
document expires immediately.  I haven't had problems with updating normal
content, but Netscape won't refresh images when they change if they are
available in the cache.

Now, there would be a useful utility:  something that resides in the system
tray and when you right-click, you can flush the memory and disk caches of
IE and Netscape.  I'll bet something like that exists...hmm...guess not
(searched both ZDnet.com and download.com).  Anyone up to the task?  Disk
caches are fairly easy, memory caches are another story.


           Thomas J. Hruska -- shinelight@crosswinds.net

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Jun 30 06:32:39 2001

Message-ID: <3B3D6477.1ED90561@rci.rutgers.edu>

> Netscape won't refresh images when they change if they are
available in the cache.

No, though there is a trick. If the Height= or Width= has
changed, NetScape thinks it is a new image. As a web-wacker you
can change Height=200 to Height=201, and see the change. But you
better change it back.

The other way is to right-click on the stale image, "Open in new
window", you'll get the stale image but shift-reload forces that
image to get fresh (without having to reload -all- the images on
the page). Then Back gets you the full page with the fresh image. 

Dennis >  I set those options long ago! 

OK, I believe you. While I rarely have problems seeing my
changes, I too have had to force it sometimes.

Are there any proxy servers or caches along the way? AOL in
particular caches pages their customers have requested, in case
another AOL user asks for the same page soon after. Thomas's
meta-tags *may* force AOL's caches to read a new copy every time
(though I thought AOL needed no-cache in the HTTP header, not the
HTML file). Other ISPs also cache to reduce load; my school had
to cache for a few months while one of the two outside lines was
down for repair and traffic on the other line was clogged.
Caching a few hundred of the student's favorite external sites
really took the edge off the overload. 

 -PRR

Comment below

Thomas J. Hruska wrote:

> As I was playing around with IE, I noticed that the headers contain some
> extremely useful data that my CGI-based applications could use.  I have
> this interesting idea that Xitami could do something horribly non-standard
> and pass all of the headers onto my CGI (filter) through another
> environment variable.  Here is what I propose:
> 
> 1)  Create a configuration file option to turn on/off the COMPLETE_HEADERS
> environment variable.
> 2)  During runtime, if the environment variable option is on, then the
> COMPLETE_HEADERS variable is created.  Xitami stores the headers into the
> environment variable as a zero-terminated URL encoded string.
> 
> Of particular interest to me (and probably a few others) are the headers:
> 
> UA-pixels: 1152x864
> UA-color: color16
> UA-OS: Windows NT
> UA-CPU: x86
> 
> Now, I could use JavaScript to do what I want on the client end of things,
> but it would be nice to just grab and parse the headers for the information

Since this is coming from a form - create a hidden field which is 
populated by Javascript. The JS can query the browser for those fields. 
This works with all browsers and is trivial to implement and you don't 
need any cookies.

For example

<form name=myForm><script>
  document.writeln('<INPUT TYPE="hidden" NAME="hiddenObject" VALUE="' +
     screen.width + "," + screen.height + "," +
     screen.pixelDepth + "," + screen.colorDepth + "'>" )
</script>
rest of form </form>

--
